when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式設計師 , 她確實做過一些事 , 但事實上 , 要說的是 , 未來要比這個更好 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現在1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械性的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是來自數學的觀點 , 但追蹤告訴我們一件很重要的事情 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基金給電腦科學 , 說: 「 不管你怎麼製作電腦科學 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你是電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像現今的電腦 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械一樣 , 像是babbage , 或電子產品 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它很小 , 所有東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 計算機率是如此 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做churchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurching
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你得到這個連結 , 你說這個東西是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以用電腦來做所有事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢 , 它有大約1k記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用punchcas , 它用punchcas , 它會用punchcas , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punchcas , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch
it did have a ram pack .	牠有一大堆羊皮包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上更多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在華盛頓 , 科學博物館的檔案中有數百個計劃和數百個計劃 , 還有數以百計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴布所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 28 」 的名字 , 也是我先前提到博物館的名字 , 也是一位慈善機構的名字 , 我開始建造出不同的引擎 , 這也是我們所謂的 「 飛行計畫 」 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會建造出分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有一些部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一 , 掃描是babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 目前正在研究所有的計畫 , 來決定如何建造 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是電腦模擬機器 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成了 , 你就得去看看這件事情 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶操作 , 我看到了記憶運作 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我知道電腦如何運作 , 但是你不得不在你面前 , 看到記憶操作 , 我看見記憶運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在我們要做模擬的時候 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫 , 他說 , 只要分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 當然 , 他從來沒有建造 , 因為他總是有新規劃 , 但在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們看一些例子 , 說明它看起來像動作的樣子 , 用影片顯示 , 只是一部分的動作 , 會讓它看起來像動作 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三組裝置 , 加上機制 , 這樣你就可以想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年之前 , 我們會有它 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 亞瑟伯特•阿曼•曼伯特祖先展示了他最近期的作品 , 描述了人類的三項最近期的作品 , 在這個圖片上 , 《地球上》、《地球上》 , 《家人》 , 這張圖片 , 《地球上》 , 《家人》 , 這張圖片是關於人類的環境 , 透過呼吸拍攝影片 , 將近期的 「 人性影像 」 和 「 家 」 描繪出來 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影師 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yann藝術husbertrand捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對這個星球上有很大的影響力 , 以飛機飛行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	在大氣層中 , 大氣層中九噸的二氧化碳是兩個大氣層的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談的是生態學 , 我把二氧化碳當作法國人一年 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我必須殺一位法國人 , 當我回到家的時候 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳排放 , 就像每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	接下來我要展示一些例子 , 是我在過去一年所做的一些例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	阿爾伯塔沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人工作的環境中 , 24個小時 , 七分之二十四小時 , 才能讓它們能做到 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但是我們每年使用三倍的石油 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁在新加勒尼亞 。

fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	漁業、養殖、養育 , 農場仍是世界上最有意義的人類 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們連結在一起的距離 , 遠比我們所能分裂的還要多 。

in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年以來 , 我們已經改善了 , 比人類的歷史還要多 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上有一半的森林已經消失 。
water resources are running low .	水資源很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	強化的土壤是剝削土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只是在嘗試改善我們的生命 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距更廣泛 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有了解到 , 比地球還快的速度 , 我們還能保持它的速度 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可行的 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston , richardsonston理查•雷斯頓所說的 , 很便宜和快速基因組定序將健康照護轉移 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學技術 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	底部是性染色體 。

so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在 , 我們要做一個基因組 , 我們將這些複製成五十個複製品 , 然後我們將這些複製體複製成五十個複製品 , 然後我們將這些複製體複製成小五十個複製品 。

now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	近年來 , 我沒有帶領人類的靈感來源 , 但我確實帶了一根骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數以萬計的病人 , 大部分的患者都有先進的氣候疾病 , 像是血液、淋巴和其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學工作 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們有個bob , 這是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他送到國家裡 , 拯救了一名兒童血管病患的白血病 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們該如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個全部的醫生 , 包括麻醉護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身上 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們帶著這個小針頭 , 你知道 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們把這個軟體組織放到硬骨頭上 , 以每次 , 針對10個骨髓 , 每次使用一次 , 針對一連串的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到護士裡 , 把牠送到海裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把我帶回來 , 我們再次做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約有200倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手臂的尾聲結束後 , 我手上有個叫聲 , 請舉手 , 舉例來說 , 我手上有一支手臂 , 讓她的手臂變得像瑞士起司一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在四十年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想了一套新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 馬爾礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	標示了它的運作方式 , 顯示出這個現象 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的視角病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	不是進入幾十次的前面 , 而是進入前面 , 進入前面 , 再次進入骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性、有彈性的管子 , 繞著它繞著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它可以讓你很快地穿過一個洞 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們能多次通過同樣的道路 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃只能得到一支針筒 , 用一種刺激劑 , 麻醉劑 , 讓它成為一種刺激 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一小段 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩個大的動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 驚訝的是 , 我們發現 , 不僅僅是骨髓 , 我們也得到骨髓的結果 , 結果是 , 我們發現 , 比一般設備更加速率的幹細胞活動率還高達十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這套裝置是fda在過去一年才被拿到的 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活病患者 , 你可以看到它遵循著彈性的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩位在同一個病患 , 同一個病患 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	由於當地麻醉劑麻醉劑量
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再次 , 我們再次增加了3到6倍的幹細胞比標準處理同樣的病患更幹細胞
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成年人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人的幹細胞在我們的骨髓中 , 包括血液幹細胞 , 包括血液幹細胞 , 在我們骨髓裡的幹細胞 , 包括我們血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 包括在我們骨髓中的血幹細胞 , 我們已經用了超過40年來的幹細胞 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 血管疾病、血管疾病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出去 , 我們剛剛出去了 , 今年 , 我們已經出了一代2.0名的排列人 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是讓更多的幹細胞轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人去尋找潛在的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可以讓你銀行自己的幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康時 , 要用在未來你需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 每一年都在史丹福大學 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這技術能讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和瑟夫•葛雷特•萊西提出了一個爭議性的新模型 , 即便是宇宙中最美麗的新模型 , 它就是你所見過最美麗的新模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科學 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , 所有東西都在他理論上 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	喔 , 去看看那些殺人的方程式 。 甜點 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘 , 我要做最好的 , 可以描述美麗的粒子物理學 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 有很多我們可以從珊瑚身上學到的東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭都有數千個個別的口袋 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些細菌會不斷地突破並分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級的珊瑚 , 我們可以獨自一個人問他一個問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們能問他該如何在這個特定的位置與鄰居相比 , 不管是哪個樣子 , 或是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	為了把溫度升高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你看到 , 我正在捕捉恐怖的捕魚 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是非常明顯的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在其他的位置也一樣 , 但 , 把它們分離為個人 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個很聰明的珊瑚會獨特地準備了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實持續分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對人類來說 , 很奇怪的是 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異 , 是由erwinschrodinger和他的貓所做的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , schrodinger是一個放射性的樣本 , 由量子力學的法律組成 , 讓它被放射性 , 和一種放射性樣本 , 由量子力學的法律組成 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本的輻射中 , 它會釋放毒素和schrdinger已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些特質是透過每個人體驗的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	如同所言 , 另一種不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為每個人都只經歷一個獨立存在 , 我們也沒有看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就像我們所有人一樣 , 像是schrodinger在這裡 , 是一種珊瑚蟲在不同的可能性下降落 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這個世界是如何運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子中出現:所有事情都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述發生什麼事 , 或無法做什麼 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理告訴我們 , 一切都經過幾何 , 和互相的交互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	但如果這些互動是完美的平衡 , 就會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來談談我們對這些粒子的了解 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個質子和反射光會被加速到接近光速和反射的光 , 產生出一堆能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上就被轉換成一系列的原子粒子 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器大型強大的撞擊器 , 由於蒙特利的大型強子撞擊器 , 將五倍的電力與蒙特利的大型強子相互作用 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何個體內產生的撞擊 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們 , 粒子是如何產生的 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有許多質量和能量 , 由質量和能量所組成 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子比這個能源限制還大了 , 還不存在我們 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼新粒子加速器很興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會將能量限制七次超越前所未有的 , 所以 , 我們將會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到之前我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	這裡有一大堆原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的人 , 許多人都能做好的生活 , 把他們推進去 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電荷和一個中央的夥伴稱之為 「 中子 」 , 沒有電荷和一個非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相反的 , 中子的質子和中子的質子和中子的質子和中子會產生質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左右和右手邊緣 , 而有反粒子相反的粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷是相同的 , 但有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和各種力量粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力電磁力與電磁力互動 , 電磁力與電磁力相互作用 , 叫做光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常弱的力量 , 相互作用的力量 , 與左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強大力量 , 引起了不同種類:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann , 這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 它的質量和旋轉是重力的力量 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解這裡有不同的指控和這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 指控每個粒子的每一個粒子都有 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	以前還沒見過的粒子 , 但是我們確保存在希格斯粒子是希格斯粒子 , 它會讓質量和其他粒子相比 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子撞擊器的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎一定會這麼做 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所能看見的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	在這個演講結束後 , 我會向各位展示一個美麗的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把這些不同的粒子用在不同的粒子上 , 用它們不同的粒子和載荷 , 有26個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子可以繼續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	似乎很奇怪 , 自然會有這麼多的元素 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們排列出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 電荷是三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它會產生一個電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是兩種其他載荷的組合:hypercharge和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把這些粒子放在這個二維空間的電荷中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的方向 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力和弱力相互作用 , 會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 不合理的推測器 」 , 它在1967年被放棄 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這些原因是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	希格斯在左邊有一個大大的質量並破壞對稱的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 , 讓弱勢力非常弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為大希格在這個圖形中 , 電磁力很大 , 電磁力和電力相互作用 , 電磁力仍然沒有大量的作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁和弱力是兩維空間中的粒子電磁和弱力 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的力量轉換成兩個載荷 , 引導引力粒子在這些方向的方向 , 引導強力的力量 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有知識粒子的電荷都可以在四維空間中 , 以維度的載荷空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子相互作用時 , 自然會維持一個完美平衡的四個方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和一顆粒子相撞 , 它會產生出能量 , 它在四個電荷中產生一股能量 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能被創造出來 , 只要它有著同樣的能量 , 並維持了零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	舉例來說 , 這個弱勢力粒子和反粒子會在撞擊中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 載荷一定總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子會被轉換成電子和一個微粒子 , 而這三個仍然加上了零 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以 , 電荷的模式不僅僅是如此 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是如何發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	在四維空間中 , 我們可以把這個載荷空間轉換為四個維度 , 讓更好的觀察強度互相作用 , 來得到更好的觀察強度的互動 , 讓它能更好地觀察強度的互動 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強大的力量中 , 比如這個綠色 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個綠色 , 用顏色標示標示 , 例如這個綠色 , 用顏色標示標示 , 例如這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動會發生在我們體內的每一秒鐘 , 把原子核聚集在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個主題對三種力量並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種引力力的力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	我們包括這些 , 每一個物質粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分裂了 , 在六度空間中提供一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以把這個模式轉換成六個維度 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們對大自然的知識建立起來 , 最好的知識是大自然如何建立在微小尺度的範圍中 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在極限的情況下 , 是我們能夠觸碰到的實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理學 , 這些微小的尺寸是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和古老的想法 , 關於我們不知道的東西 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式使用數學 , 看看我們能否把這個模式運用數學 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 來讓我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 我們希望用這張圖來預測新粒子 , 來預測新粒子時 , 我們會看到實驗達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有一個古老的概念 , 叫做 「 希格斯粒子 」 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中 , 和希格斯粒子相互作用 , 來產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的力量 , 來引導新方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們向新方向提出新方向時 , 我們猜測荷粒子在這個方向的方向 , 我們會猜測荷粒子在哪個方向 , 然後我們就可以和他人一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜想 , 我們能在六個荷荷維度中建立標準荷荷 , 由六個荷荷維度所組成的對稱性 , 將標準載荷量提升到六個載荷中 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 這個特定的選擇應對一個偉大的理論 , 由巴黎和薩爾姆在1973年提出 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新的獨立模式 , 我們可以看到一些差距 , 粒子似乎是錯失了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是 「 合理工作 」 的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家看起來更大、更大、更多的對稱模式 , 包括建立模式 , 包括建立模式 , 包括建立模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測出存在粒子從未見過的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統計模型預測了兩個新力量的存在 , 它應該和弱勢力相互作用 , 只是弱勢力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以在七維空間中 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實:第二 , 第三代的載荷 , 和第三代物質的載荷相同 , 以七維空間為第一代 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨特的 , 由六個電荷組成的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準的電荷空間中 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 若我們在八度空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以為每一個粒子創造出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以把這八個維度放進去 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一個世代相互聯繫 , 叫做 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中 , 它是數學中最美麗的幾何結構 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大型式的圖案之一 , 百分之十八 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊組是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案的對稱是非常複雜和美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這八種形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦相對論的一小部分 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 形狀的幾何形狀描述所有宇宙如何運作在最微小的尺度 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀存在於八維空間中 , 這形狀的形狀是非常美麗的 , 而且它總結了數千種可能的交互作用 , 這種複雜形狀的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他的細微的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	在一個特定的旋轉中 , 我們可以透過這個圖案 , 看到所有粒子 , 通過這個模式 , 在八維空間中 , 透過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 , 通過這個模式 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 只要我們看到一些洞 , 新粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子有20個落差 , 新粒子被稱為patisalam粒子 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子會像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色和強力的力量 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填寫這些新的粒子 , 給予我們全部的新粒子 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個偉大的數學美麗可以描述真相相互作用的真相 , 最小的尺度是很棒的數學 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然所描述的數學並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略曾寫過: 「 大自然的書 , 一直在於數學的本質 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形、圓圈和其他幾何形狀 , 不論是哪個字 , 都無法理解一個單一字 , 而在黑暗的黑暗實驗室裡 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真實的 , 我也試著跟伽利略說的數學粒子物理學用三角形、圓圈和其他幾何形式來描述數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我一起工作時 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的心臟是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 一個美麗的圖案 , 數量子力學 , 這個數學描述了宇宙 , 以一個美麗的形式 , 來呈現出一個美麗的模式 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的圖案 , 使用新的機器 , 像是大型強強強強的強強強強強硬體 , 我們可能可以觀察到 , 大型強子對撞機是大型強大的撞擊器 , 我們可能可以觀察到 , 大型強子對撞機
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現的是一個很棒的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc發現粒子在這個e8圖案中 , 會很酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 很有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但不符合這個模式 , 這會非常有趣 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是很糟糕的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那麼 , 該是多麼糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作是非常冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的 , 都是很長的拍攝 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	許多努力都知道 , 大部分這些想法都可能不會結束對自然的影響 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論 , 像是:有許多大爆炸 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這個理論上 , 新物理理論就像是新公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有大量的投資 , 就會很難放棄一線的研究 , 不論是怎麼做 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果你沒有工作 , 你得要去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持保健的方法是保持保健和觀點 , 才能保持健康和永續性 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我曾嘗試過最好的生活 , 能活平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生命 , 和我自己三個載荷的方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	順便一提 , 儘管我在物理學上工作 , 我仍然知道我已經活過了好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十多年來 , 我住在土地 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在這是宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 是我的父母 , 我如何經常生活 , 卻沒有參與任何全職工作 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我將讓你們進入這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我家在maui的景觀 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能注意到這些美麗的景觀很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。

but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租容讓我花時間去做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在美麗的地方 , 生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 並且保持平衡 。

africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲 , 動物 , 生物多樣性 , 環境 , 全球問題 , 污染 , 生物多樣性 , 環境 , 全球問題 , 污染 , 生物多樣性 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍妮•哈拉爾幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 午安 , 不好 。

that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺時所做的 。

and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天我想跟大家談談這個晚點 , 昨天就在昨天發生了 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這令人驚奇的三歲小孩 , 伊斯蘭教徒 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過了人類的歷史 , 家族樹 , 人類的歷史 , 家族樹 , 由dna基因遺傳傳遞 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這位是古生物學家 , 拉特•萊特 , 他在我研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在那之後 , 非常了不起 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這很普遍 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲的早期人類的遺骸 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以告訴很多關於那些從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中從化石中所看到的形狀 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化化 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在 , 很常見的理論是 , 如果我們找到行為模式類似或相同 , 在我們最親近的親戚中 , 人類的祖先 , 大約七百萬年前 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經把這些特徵和我們從古老的古老古老古老的古老人帶走了 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今天的教科書和人類演化的行為 , 你通常會發現有人在考慮人類進化的行為 , 你通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們在ted會議中聽到了這個ted會議 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我也要留言 , 讓黑猩猩對我們的行為有興趣 , 讓黑猩猩就像我們一樣 , 牠們的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十歲 , 儘管我們認為大多數人可能不會在野生中六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	女先生 , 她的第一個寶寶在11或12歲時 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	此外 , 她有一個嬰兒 , 只有每五或六年 , 一個嬰兒的年齡 , 只有每五或六年 , 有一個嬰兒的年齡 , 只有一個嬰兒 , 和媽媽在晚上睡覺時 , 和媽媽一起睡覺 , 和母親一起睡覺 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 這很長一段時間 , 對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 因為我們對黑猩猩來說 , 就是對黑猩猩來說 , 就是對黑猩猩來說 , 就是對黑猩猩 ,
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦變得更複雜 , 在不同類型的動物身上 , 我們發現 , 學習在演化中扮演更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察牠們的老虎 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們可以模仿行為的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這樣 , 我們相信 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 我們相信 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習的行為 , 我們就能描述這些工具的行為 , 成為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有語音 。 我們談到這一點 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們有非常豐富的重複性 , 相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至在相同的情況下 , 相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 甚至在相同的情況下 , 相似的 , 甚至是相似的 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們也吻合手 , 抓住手 , 抓住手 , 把手放在背上 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們會搖滾 , 搖滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多例子 , 包括同情心、追求愛和真實的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們就像我們一樣 , 牠們有黑暗的面向 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們是極殘酷的 , 甚至是原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些真正的侵略性行為 , 主要是對鄰居社會團體的行為 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們是非常激進人心的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有線條 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是個非常模糊的循環 , 隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 它會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究 , 一直持續到那天 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 牠們的複雜社交生活在野外 , 讓我們了解到我們是沒有分離的 , 和我們分享地球的動物有多大 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 都會失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這張照片是從空氣中拍攝的 , 它給你展示森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時 , 我在1960年的時候 , 一直在我腦海裡浮現 , 在這整個區域 , 大約十六年前 , 我在公園的東岸 , 發現在公園的東岸 , 當時 , 一個問題來到我腦海裡 , 在那裡 , 大約十六年前 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園 , 試圖拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園時 , 他們會掙扎生存嗎 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	越來越多人住在土地 , 可能支援不足 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量增加了來自於巴基斯坦的難民營 , 以及從巴基來的數字 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們無法負擔購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常平凡的改善生活在公園的人們生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從小到12個村莊 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去探究 , 但它包含了像樹木護士 , 這種方法 , 幾乎是沙漠的土地 , 像樹木護士 , 幾乎是沙漠的土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、防止土壤消耗 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建土地的農耕地 , 兩年後 , 可以再一次生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民從水中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小群的婦女合作 , 為微貸款提供機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們在全世界的情況下 , 大約有95%的貸款都被回收 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 她們可以完成第二課 , 在明顯了解世界各地 , 女性教育 , 女性教育 , 提供獎學金 , 讓女性教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 她們可以完成第二課 , 在明顯的了解中 , 世界各地都有女性教育 , 提供獎學金 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計劃 , 有些東西在保育 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育農民住在這些24個村落裡的農民生活在這個村落裡 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一系列的農夫 , 但當我們開始研究一系列的農夫 , 其實是坦尚尼亞人來研究一系列的農夫 , 而不是看著我們 , 一群白人來研究一系列的農夫 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	它是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民們談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對教育有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間進步 , 他們開始了解更多關於保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 在山丘上高層的山丘是樹木 , 所以你有很糟糕的土壤漏油和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展出我們稱之為 「 更偉大的地球生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這裡是國家公園 , 擴展到各國公園 , 延伸到全國公園 , 延伸到全國公園 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村落有更好的標準 , 他們真的同意將近百分之二十的土地在公園裡 , 再次再一次 , 樹木會長回來 , 黑猩猩會有更好的標準 , 牠們可以旅行 , 與其它獨立的土地相互交流 , 再次 , 樹木會長回來 , 黑猩猩會有更好的標準 , 牠們可以旅行 , 來與其它獨立的土地相互交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲各地的其他地方 , 和極端族群一起複製它 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們已經討論過了幾天 , 主要的問題是 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮很大 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	一旦你砍掉了大量的土壤 , 絕大多數的人住在土地上 , 不是肥沃 , 特別是當你砍伐樹木 , 將土壤打開 , 讓土壤開放 , 讓土壤開放 , 讓土壤開放 , 讓土壤開放 , 希望人們能為自己和家人做些什麼 , 要怎麼做呢 ? 要怎麼做 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題不僅是非洲 , 而是發展中國家的其他地方 , 還在哪裡 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	各位知道 , 有名的科學家 , 艾.威爾森說 , 如果在這個星球上每個人 , 都需要三個新的行星 , 我們就需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說了四個 。 但我們沒有它們 。 我們有了一顆 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	接下來發生了什麼事呢 ? 我是說 , 在這裡 , 我們要問的是 , 世界上最有智慧的人 , 就是我們有史以來最聰明的行星 , 地球上有著這種特殊的大腦 , 可以用這些ted會議來討論 , 但我們要摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了一個重大決策之前 , 坐下來問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們七代前代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決定 , 我不是特別談論非洲 , 而是開發中國家主要的決策 , 包括數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 會如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行時 , 我了解到許多非洲的問題 , 如我所面臨的 , 許多非洲的問題 , 都能被黑猩猩和它們消失的森林所吸引 , 我了解到更多 , 許多非洲的問題可能是被黑猩猩和它們消失的森林所造成的 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始旅行在非洲 , 談話 , 在歐洲 , 談話 , 在美國 , 進入亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在談的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在污染我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水水可能是世界上最關鍵的議題之一 , 我們會面臨的問題 , 包括農業、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 仍然在世界各地都被污染 , 不論是哪裡都被污染、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 都被污染在這個世紀 , 和家庭的化學物質仍然在世界各地都被污染了 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍掉 , 海嘯變得更糟糕 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤問題 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們還有其他溫室氣體的排放 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都開始相信 , 我們的氣候變遷會造成問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混合起來 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會受到更糟的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經被影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨水發生時 , 它通常會導致洪水、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在這個地區的人口數量 , 沒有人會因為整個土地被降低 , 無法消費 , 因為整個土地都被降低 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的裂縫 , 直到最後一棵樹木被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只是在非洲 , 而是世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 讓我驚訝的是 , 當我在旅行時 , 我遇到了許多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可能有某種差異的大腦 , 這種特別聰明的大腦 , 特別聰明的大腦 , 這種特殊的大腦 , 這種特殊的大腦 , 這種特殊的大腦 , 這種特殊的大腦呢 ? 談論在非科學領域 , 愛和同情心 , 卻有某種差異嗎 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們談話時 , 基本上他們說的是 「 不論是憂鬱症、愛情 」 或 「 愛情 」 , 意思是 , 他們說的是 「 不論 」 或 「 我們感覺到 」 , 因為我們覺得你已經對抗了我們的未來 , 而我們卻沒有什麼可以做的事 。
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥善了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 我覺得這張美麗的星球 , 每當我看著他們 , 我覺得這絕望是絕望的 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這引發了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根和芽 , 它開始在坦尚尼亞 , 並且現在在坦尚尼亞已經散播到97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根源是符合的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊的陽光很小 , 可以破壞牆壁 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	看到磚牆 , 所有這些問題都在地球上、環境和社會上 , 都是希望的 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數十萬個年輕人 , 都可以打破 , 讓這個更美好的世界變成更好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根和芽的最重要訊息:每個人每一天都有改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們在這個房間裡有選擇 , 我們有選擇 , 在這個房間裡 , 我們有選擇 , 想要做些什麼樣的差別 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 這樣我們才能改變窮人的選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選擇三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於他們是哪個國家 , 不管是城市或鄉村 , 還是鄉村 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有計畫從幼稚園到大學 , 有更多成年人開始自己的根源和槍枝 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 三種不同的不同問題 , 彼此之間互相連結和衝突 , 才能讓這個更好的世界 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一個項目就是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能幫助他們 , 他們可能會募資金錢幫助全世界各地的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項項目就是要幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 也是動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個項目就是幫助我們所有人共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	最後 , 所有這些都是學習的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區 , 在我們的家庭 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭 , 我們社區中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 與我們之間的關係 , 和諧 。

we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這個星球還要多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只有在坦尚尼亞、南非、加拿大、哥巴茲尼亞、南非、加拿大、哥巴茲尼亞、南非、百分之九十七的國家 , 我說 , 世界上有97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們正在種植樹木 , 他們正在種植樹木 。 他們正在種植樹木 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營裡工作 , 把雞蛋花在難民營裡 , 把雞蛋花在難民營裡 , 讓雞蛋花一點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵養他們的家人 , 感到驕傲和強迫 , 因為他們不再有助益 , 並且依賴其他的蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助 , 來給予一些心理協助 。

it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它啟發了我 , 最後的兩天之內 , 我們已經聽過這句話了 。 最後的兩天之內 , 人類精神的堅韌性 , 人類精神的韌性 , 那些你認為會被貧窮、或疾病或疾病所侵蝕的人 , 或其他的 , 可以把他們自己放進去 , 讓那些你認為會被貧窮、或疾病或疾病 , 或任何人 , 可以把他們自己從來 , 帶給他們一部分 , 去改變世界 。

ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 在奈及利亞 , 全世界的大型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都嘗試過他們最好 , 卻被執行 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人很鼓舞人心 。

and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一句話說 , 今天我遇到了這位女子 , 她正在跑這整個研討會中心 。

and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常令人興奮的是 , 希望明天 , 當他們被賦予權力時 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真正是希望明天的機會 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家diannacohen分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真相 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 以及我們的生活中有一些關於塑膠污染的真相 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	狄安娜•柯芬:粗糙的真相 , 關於塑膠污染 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是一個視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中之一 , 塑膠污染協會 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在用塑膠袋 , 用塑膠袋 , 將我和塑膠袋融合在一起 , 將我和塑膠袋子結合在一起 , 將我和塑膠袋子結合在一起 , 過去二十年來 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們轉換成二、三維的雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	過去八年間 , 我的工作開始分裂 , 分裂成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	對於塑膠而言 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分裂成小小一點點 , 因為它總是仍然塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們所發現的是 , 在海洋環境中 , 許多東西都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去的幾年裡 , 我了解了太平洋垃圾堆和gyre 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我的第一個反應 , 是我的第一個反應 , 我想這是很多人的第一個反應 , 就是: 「 喔 ! 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去那裡和清潔這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的開發了一個提議 , 要用一艘拖車機、一台拖車機、一台拖車機、一台機器 , 和一台超級機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 把塑膠拆解 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠黏起來 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 , 把塑膠變成垃圾桶 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和當地人聊天聊天 , 研究塑膠問題在海洋環境中 , 我開始跟大家談談 , 實際上 , 要回頭看看更大的圖片 。 我真的需要回頭看更大的圖像 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個方法 , 來轉移假裝 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切除單純和可塑膠的塑膠 , 每天都在全球規模上 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 我也了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只擔心塑膠 , 你想要想像在太平洋中間的塑膠 , 我已經知道現在有11個塑膠 , 可能是塑膠 , 在五大洋中 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是塑膠的塑膠 , 我很擔心它是塑膠的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我去超級市場 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠上 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均都包裝在塑膠上 , 甚至在健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也擔心在冰箱裡的塑膠和毒素從塑膠變成我們的身體 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以 , 我和一群其他的人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫 , 但有些是非常基本的 。

in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細看 , 尤其是在塑膠瓶子裡 , 大部分只會被丟棄 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環再利用 , 塑膠瓶可以再一次塑膠瓶蓋瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶也不會再被塑膠瓶蓋瓶了 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在想的事情 , 就是拒絕 , 請大家想想我們已經把第四個面向前面放到: 「 減少、回收、回收 」 、 「 減少、回收 」 、 「 減少、回收 」 。

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里斯•羅德里 , 和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都在世貿易中心攻擊中 , 發現和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都在尋找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都在尋找和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都在尋找和平 , 牠們是為了找到和平 , 牠們是為了找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽都在尋找和平 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11:那些發現原諒、友誼的人 。

we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否有直到36小時後 。

and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 可怕的爆炸 , 在我們的生命中 , 很糟糕的爆炸 , 很糟糕的爆炸 , 我們的生活中不可怕的爆炸 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指控在六種反對的案例中 , 例如 , 美國政府稱之為死刑 , 如果被告知 , 我的丈夫 , 和我對他說話 , 不論 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過人類權利團體 , 我們和其他受害者的家人聚在一起 。

someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要和那個女人當我比較強壯 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍在深深的悲慟中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。

because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為當有人聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我得到立即的同情心 。

so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月2002年11月 , 艾莎會告訴你們該怎麼做 。

before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生活品之前 , 最好的手濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會穿透200奈米的細菌 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	最小的病毒 , 另一方面是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以 , 這絕對是在200奈米的洞見中 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生活品質是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	一切都沒有發生 。

paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 詩人寫了一首詩 , 名為英國詩人 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教科爾的腦袋裡出現了 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是: 「 夏天 , 我聽到一個很遠的距離 , 越來越低、越來越低 , 越來越大的聲音 , 遠遠在地下 , 流流 , 大聲說 , 我聽到一個遙遠的、親近的、親近的、親近的、親近的、親近的、親愛的朋友 , 和食物聚在一起 , 快到死去 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩人有興趣的詩人是 「 shropshirelad 」 , 詩是《shropshirelad》 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但波爾斯人的觀點是 , 如同你所聽到的 , 尤其是當權力改變時 , 十九世紀的西班牙人會接觸到我們 , 並且將要進入一個非常恐怖的時代 , 歷史的歷史力量改變 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士們 , 女士們先生們 , 全都被暴動 , 許多人都不受傷害 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你們的信息是 , 我相信我們已經被告知了 , 如果你喜歡 , 生活在那一刻 , 在歷史上 , 建立了新勢力的新勢力 , 已經開始改變和新勢力 , 來改變和新世界的新勢力 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是我們現在看到的很明顯 , 通常是非常嚴重的時期 , 通常是很明顯的 , 常常血腥的時期 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 每一世紀都發生了 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 最後一次發生了 , 同情心的力量 , 來自古老的國家 , 歐洲的大西洋 , 到美國的新興發權力 , 過去發生了 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在這個時代 , 歐洲權力被用來當作戰場 , 第二部分是:兩場大戰 , 世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	馬歐文戰爭在歐洲內戰中 , 可能更準確地描述它們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士們 , 我們生活在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我想談談三種因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者 , 首先是改變權力 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些新維度我想要從未曾發生過的即將發生的新維度
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	咱們來談談關於改變權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的情況是 , 很恐怖的是 , 因為從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到一些稍微不同的改變 , 俄羅馬和權力轉變在歐洲文明時期發生 , 但在歐洲文明中 , 我們也看到了一些不同的事情 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是從國家到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也在移動垂直 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今 , 國內的權力已經被擴大 , 以致於國內的權力被擴展 , 被監禁 , 國內的權力被監禁 , 被監禁在國際舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談論全球化的全球化 , 但事實上這是全球化的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國際舞台上 , 國際舞台上 , 國際舞台上 , 沒有任何權力 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球階段 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 網路的權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台 , 權力 , 國際舞台和全球階段的力量 , 實際上 , 國際舞台和全球階段的力量 , 多國際舞台的權力 , 大多國際舞台和全球階段的力量 , 其實 , 國際舞台和全球性階段的力量 , 如今 , 大量的金錢改革者 , 將我們所有人的權力轉移到膝蓋上 , 即便如此 , 他們的權力已經將我們所有人的權力轉換成金錢的力量 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球空間 , 不被規定法律的規則 , 也不被規定法律的規則 , 而那些人可能會自由地限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這套裝置強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是為了讓那些有權力的人在太空中沒有限制的權力 , 但在歷史的過程中 , 沒有限制 , 不管是 , 規律的規律 , 都沒有限制 , 不管是在哪裡 , 都沒有限制 , 不管是在哪裡 , 都沒有限制 , 只需要國際貿易、網際網路等等 , 等等 , 那些有權力在太空空間中沒有限制的 , 只需要國際貿易、網際網路等等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的重點是 , 即使你是世界上最強大的國家 , 不論你是地球上最強大的國家 , 不論是誰 , 都可以攻擊你 , 即使你是世界上最強大的國家 , 不論你是地球上最有力的國家 , 甚至是地球上最有力的國家 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	意思是說 , 有60%的4000萬美元被送到9/11 , 被摧毀了 , 9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 網際網路、衛星廣播 , 來探究我們的系統和我們的方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久之後 , 歷史的規則是 , 歷史的規則是權力管理要遵守的規則 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信這一點 , 那就是我們時間的挑戰之一 , 就是全球化的力量 , 那麼 , 接下來 , 我們時間的挑戰之一就是將治理轉向全球化 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 數十年來 , 我們的前進 , 將會成為一個更大、更少的社會 , 我們能夠達成目標 , 來促進全球的空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意到 , 我不是在談論政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談論一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我的觀點是 , 各位先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 這不太可能發生在聯合國機構裡 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得要發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際的鼓舞 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個意義 , 就是你可以合法國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當它來到全球政策時 , 我猜猜的是 , 這不會發生在聯合國和國內機構中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 它會被強大的力量結合在一起 , 建立基礎的系統、協議 , 來管理全球的空間 。

now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們將會再回來 , 假如你把最強大的力量集合起來 , 把最強大的力量集合起來 , 來填補管理空間 , 那麼 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個很大的問題 , 我們會再回到這一秒 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些殘酷的事件 , 或更不穩定 , 我們的成功會在大量的狀態下 , 我們的成功 , 會大量地仰賴我們的能力 , 來讓全球空間變得更不穩定 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看看這開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟聽眾像這樣的話題 , 但權力不只是轉變 , 而是轉變平面 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說 , 歷史文明 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史文明 , 文明的歷史文明 , 在大西洋的歷史文明 , 被文明的歷史文明化 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的是基本的轉變 , 遠離國民聚集在太平洋岸邊 。

my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我想 , 值得注意的是 , 美國在未來10年 , 十五歲時 , 仍然是世界上最強大的國家 , 但它的背景 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們在五十年內 , 最不尋常的時刻 , 和我們所處的環境一樣 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 也是我們所擁有的全球 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 都需要被它的位置 , 來到華盛頓世界 , 到華盛頓一個世界最不尋常的地方 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這並不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在新興的情況是歷史上最常見的情況 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多點世界的新興 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國已經成為我們世界的主要特徵 。

and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	然後你開始看到在中國的替代方案 , 當然 , 雖然我的猜測是中國 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是中國 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是中國 , 當然 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是 , 中國的平均高度不是平均的 。

europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	在19世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外國秘書 , 被用來描述它是 " 歐洲人的權力 "
