britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎與柏林聯合在一起 , 巴黎會聚集在一起 , 維納和羅馬來提供一個平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在 , 注意到 , 在這個日期中 , 你有固定的聯合國 , 維持世界 , 你有固定的聯盟 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的政權 , 意味著修復政權 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力有多重力力意味著轉變和轉變 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們會越來越了解我們的盟友不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	英國外國秘書館說: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密曾說過: 「 英國外國秘密曾說: 「 英國外國秘密曾說: 「 英國外國秘密會說: 「 英國外國秘密

note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意一下 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 不夠好 , 要讓西方獨自一人 , 我們得要把其他人帶進去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須帶出這個案例 , 阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試圖去做自己的時候 , 我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜猜是20世紀末 , 我們到了400年之久 , 因為它是西方力量的西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方力量、西方國家的力量 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方世界各個角落 , 都可以提出和缺失 。
but that's no longer true .	但這不再是真實的 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最後的金融危機為例 , 在第二次世界大戰結束 。

i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到達了400年 , 西方力量已經夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會在世界各地和平流行 。 」

how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色背景下 , 保持在藍色的旗子裡 , 保持在藍色的旗子裡 , 保留在藍色的旗子裡 , 保留在藍色旗子裡 ?

the chinese naval contingent .	中國的中文字母 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是一家國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要維持海車開放 。

it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的不同方式 , 來看看這個世界現在正在出現 。

today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在現代世界中 , 因為網路 , 因為這些人在談論的 , 一切都與一切有關 。

but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們很親密地聚集在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥灣流入墨西哥 , 它是個問題 , 查爾斯在墨西哥 , 查爾斯在墨西哥為查爾斯號航空24小時 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷赫曼兄弟走下 , 全都崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的暴風雨 , 非洲的暴風雨 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地深深地互相連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	那就意味著 , 國家獨立行動的概念 , 不是和其他人合作 , 而是沒有與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 , 而非與他人合作 , 而非與其他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為 , 國內國家的權利不足 , 國家本身也不足以控制自己的領土 , 因為在國內國家的行動 , 已經開始影響到他們內在國家的權力 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是一位年輕士兵 , 在英國的小帝國戰爭中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	當時 , 我國家的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時敵人就在牆壁上 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁中 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談國內的安全性 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為糧食安全是安全的威脅 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為糧食安全是安全的威脅 , 我必須和政府談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家所造成的衝擊 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我的國家造成的威脅 , 我必須和大眾談談 , 因為糧食安全是對我國內的恐怖攻擊 , 為了我們的敵人 , 我們要談到國內的恐怖攻擊 , 我們已經進入了我的國家 , 在那裡 , 我們的內城有直接的效應 , 和我們從網路戰場中所見到的幾分之一 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是美國國家的安全性 , 只是為了軍人和國防部長的安全 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖在一起它的制度 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴了你一件很重要的事情 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 指揮結構 , 完全是錯的 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業知道 , 我們的典型結構 , 各位先生 , 女士們先生們 , 這是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你的能力 , 包括你的政府和外界 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	所以這是第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 如果有第三條法律 , 不要再問我 , 第一條法律和第二個法律 , 因為我還沒發明過 , 但它總是聽起來更好 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shown第三法律是 , 在現代時代 , 所有東西都連結在一起 , 最重要的事情是 , 你能做什麼 , 和其他人有關 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是 , 無論你是政府 , 不管你是軍隊 , 不管你是企業 , 你的網絡 , 和其他人的關係 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在產業中 , 政府也不會這麼做 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是 , 各位 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 我們將彼此連結在一起 , 以一種方式從未曾發生過同樣的事 , 但這也是我們與彼此相同的案件 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 首次 , 集體防禦部門 , 把我們當作概念 , 來保護我們的國家 , 不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我安全 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 , 比起他們的國 , 我安全 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是這個案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結和大規模毀滅性武器的規模破壞 , 就是 , 越來越多 , 我與敵人分享了我的敵人 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	我在1970年代 , 和蘇聯的外科醫學院談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解了我們與蘇聯的聯繫 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不足夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都意識到 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東的一個大障礙 , 和平在中東是兩邊 , 和平 , 都是以色列 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們分享集體的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 正是公共政策所扮演的角色 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩中開始 , 最後是一首詩 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐納的一首詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把貝殼賣給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個人的死亡都影響了我 , 不管誰是誰 , 都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•尼 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們的一部分是為了我們的生存而生存的 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	若要找到長壽命和生活方式的道路 , dnadnbuetner和研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 它分享了9種共同飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在tedxt上播放時 , 他分享了9種共同飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們花過去一百年 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuett:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做丹尼•泰丁的研究發現 , 只有10%的人生活在某些生物限制中 , 我們的基因會被遺傳 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是被我們生活方式所控制的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的可能性:如果我們能找到最佳生活方式 , 我們能找到最佳的生命方式 , 以便我們能找到最佳的生活方式 , 以便我們能找到最佳的生活方式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人平均壽命的最佳形式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或者是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生oz告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重點是 , 有很多混亂 , 使我們活得更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃吃有機肉嗎 ? 還是要吃肉 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	到供應食品時 , 應該要帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙又是如何呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的的目的是要讓它變成它嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性嗎 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們的研究方法是要找到四個人口統計的區域 , 來找出四個人口統計的區域 , 來找出四個人口統計 , 來找出四個人口統計 , 來找出四個國家地理位置 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一群專家帶到專家們 , 去了解這些人做的事 , 將跨越文化的分解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們 , 究竟是什麼樣的 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我要去探討一些常見的迷思 , 到長壽時期 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一種迷思是 , 如果你試著真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 僅僅僅僅僅僅僅僅有5000人在美國生活中 , 只有15000人 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快的人口統計數字 , 很難達到百分之一 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們並不是為了長壽而生長 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功的成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家說: 「 年齡是你孩子的年齡 , 和你的孩子有孩子時 , 另一個世代 。 」
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	經過演化之後的效果完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 或一隻大象 , 或人類 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要讓它到達100歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也必須得到基因學 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止衰老 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有99個可以讓我們做的事 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球 , 軟骨 , 打破你的軟骨 , 軟骨從來沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的大腦可以發揮連結 , 我們的大腦可以用白斑 , 我們的大腦可以穿上皮膚 , 我們的大腦可以發揮 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要走錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 其中有35兆個細胞 , 叫做 「 t 」 。 我們正在談論國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年 , 這種細胞會自動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己弄到某些損傷後 , 就會損害 , 損害就會損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它建立了指數 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像是垃圾時 , 我們都拍了一首歌唱片 , 讓朋友們複製這首歌曲線 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製了那首曲子的錄音帶 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製了一套錄音機 , 讓朋友們複製了那首歌劇的複製 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞中 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼 , 65倍的速度比一個125倍的速度快到125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 若你無法做些什麼 , 除非你的老化 , 或停止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是 , 最重要的是 , 科學告訴我們 , 人類身體、身體、身體 , 大約90年 , 多一點一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條線上 , 我們離開了12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們都能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部分的慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病都不夠 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 最好的方法就是去看這些世界的文化 , 讓這些年齡的人口數十年來 , 比我們更好的情況 , 中年死亡率的數量是 , 中年人口的數量 , 比我們活到的百分之十倍之多 , 中年齡死亡率是四分之一 , 中年死亡率是最好的 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們找到了我們的第一個藍色區域 , 大約在西元前125英里 , 在義大利的海岸 , 在義大利的海岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約是140萬人 , 但只有在高地上 , 島嶼就有140萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 男人住在最長的地區 , 比我們在美國這裡有百分之十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡是人們不只到達100歲的地方 , 他們也做得很好 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 有102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 樹木 , 甚至可以打敗一個60歲的孩子 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史真的回到了關於克里斯多德的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一塊古老的文化 , 被孤立了 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是牧羊 , 大量是牧羊 , 它們主要是牧羊 , 牠們主要是牧羊 , 大量是牧羊 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是植物為基礎的飲食 , 可以帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	牠們來到一個叫做卡塔卡塔音樂的麵包 , 由草食動物組成的 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 比任何葡萄糖的葡萄糖更高 , 一種葡萄酒 , 一種葡萄酒 , 含有三種葡萄糖的葡萄糖 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 含有三種葡萄糖的葡萄糖 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 含有三種葡萄糖 , 而一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何葡萄酒還多 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密 , 就是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會的一部分 , 就是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎高峰24歲 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 年紀越多的智慧 , 你就得到了更多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你在沙丁尼亞看到的月曆 , 而不是看到月曆的百分之八十 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 對於老年人的父母來說 , 這些家庭的預期壽命率下降了大約四到六年的壽命研究顯示 , 對於這些家庭的孩子來說 , 這些家庭的預期壽命比較低 , 那些家庭的死亡率和降低率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現在地球另一邊的藍色區域 , 大約800英里南 , 南方到達西島 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島嶼 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主要島嶼的北部 , 這裡是地球的二氧化碳 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這裡是最古老的居住女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是一個地方 , 在那裡 , 人們在世界上最長的壽命無法預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們生活很長一段時間 , 很快地 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性愛上 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比平均壽命更長了七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	其中一個第五分之一是乳癌和乳癌 , 在美國 , 大型殺人 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化對這些數字建議很強烈 , 讓他們能教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物的飲食 , 很多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的美國人 , 和美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是 , 他們吃的食物是怎麼吃的 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種各式各樣的策略 , 以保持遠離 , 如你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略是:他們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以他們會吃少數的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	而不是服務家人 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把食物帶到桌上 , 把食物放到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的年齡 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由於混亂所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食習慣 , 例如:哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、漢堡 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是一個小說 , 有人說在他們的胃口中 , 要提醒他們不要吃他們的胃 , 只剩下百分之八十 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	花了半小時才能從你的大腦傳送到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	只要記住停止80%的幫助 , 就能幫助你繼續做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞一樣 , okinawa有一些社會結構 , 讓我們能與長壽的聯繫 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立殺死了 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只剩下一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 生在哈拉瓦 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你會自動地有半個數十個朋友 , 和你一起旅行的人生 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 馬拉松 」 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 你總是有一位有著你的背後的人 , 會有你的回饋 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特定的媽媽 , 這五位女士已經聚在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把我們的成人分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們有工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	基本上 , 這就意味著退休到亞利桑那州的高爾夫球場 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在科納瓦語中 , 甚至沒有一個詞為退休 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反的 , 這個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗糙地翻譯 , 意思是: 「 早上你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	為了這個102歲的親戚 , 他的kigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigaikigai在
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁民而言 , 每週都要捕魚魚 , 持續為他家三次的魚類 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國家研究院 , 真的給了我們一個問卷 , 給了這些百分之百的人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們非常文化化 , 人們會問他們 , 他們是非常文化化的 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很早就知道為什麼他們在早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這個102歲的老婦女 , 她的愛吉加爾是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分離了101年半 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 感覺如何保持一位曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要求我去找美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一旦我們去看了尼蘇達州 , 那裡有非常高的比例 , 在那裡 , 那裡有非常高的百分比 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再把數據轉換了 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們找到了美國最長壽的族群之一 , 住在洛馬琳達 , 加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	抗議者是保守派的 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們從星期五日落到星期五日落的日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的監獄》 , 他們稱之為 「 時間之下 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 讓他們很長壽 , 相對的 , 比較說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的預期壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 對於一位阿德佛主義女性來說 , 他們的壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異更大 , 比起美國人數更高 , 他們預期壽命比他們的美國人數還要多 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這是一項研究 , 追蹤了約七萬人 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴謹的研究 , 我認為它最主要說明了這個藍色區塊計畫的承諾 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個不可思議的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 讓他們遵循儀式的習慣 , 通常他們會遵循儀式的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中得到他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:章魚:章魚 , 百分之三十二的綠色植物 , 絕大多數是肉類 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅的時候 , 認真看待這條聖經 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論有多忙 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注於他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在這個宗教中 , 大自然行走 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量是 , 每週一次生活的時間都沒有用過 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	每個人都不需要錢 。 不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	阿德維主義者也傾向於與其他的抗爭者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去到阿德佛派你看不見的派對 , 你不會看到人們穿著jimbeam , 或轉換個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們祈禱 , 是的 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們影響彼此對彼此的影響 , 更加深遠且可測量的方式 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 被賦予了埃爾沃爾斯沃爾斯的文化 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswhareharehareham97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬富翁 , 但當收入者想要六千美元 , 建立隱私的財務時 , 他說: 「 要賺錢 , 我會這樣做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 在接下來的三天 , 他穿著刺激的水泥 , 包圍著周圍的環境 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的是 , 也許 , 在第四天他結束了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的人 , 做開心手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 他仍然有20個開頭手術每個月都有 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 老鼠 , 十三歲 , 一隻活躍的牛仔褲 , 每天早上游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末 , 他喜歡放進板子上 , 丟下烤箱 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從那天起起 , 開始了她的日子 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在聖伯丁諾自由路上 , 在那裡她還是志願者有七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾在19個艱難的旅行中 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一你會見過的人 , 他在撒哈拉沙漠的街道上沒有陽光 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你們 , 沒有冒險比起火星大廈的冒險更駭人 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 。 」 她跟我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們所做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們就把它降到九點 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們做了兩項更藍色的區域 , 由這些常見的調節 , 和這些共同的點子發掘出來 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我是要把這句話放在這裡 , 沒有任何練習 , 至少我們思考運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反的 , 他們建立了他們的生命 , 這樣他們就不斷地被增進實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些一百歲的兒童都在地上下下 , 她們坐在地板上 , 每天有30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟旅行、教堂、或教堂 , 或朋友的家裡 , 都會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做房子工作或房子 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這種燃燒的卡路里就好像跑跑跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們都傾向於走路 , 唯一的證明方法就是他們喜歡走路 , 唯一證明了認知衰退的過程 , 並且他們都傾向於走路 , 唯一證明了認知衰退的過程 。 他們往往有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式做正確 , 所以他們有權利的權利 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每種文化都需要時間轉移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 七天的聖戰士祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先的靈感 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在心血管疾病時 , 會觸發出一種叫做 「 氣味反應 」 的反應 , 這與所有疾病有關聯邦血管疾病的相關性反應 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來十五分鐘 , 就會變成更加抗炎狀態的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有用詞語來描述 , 像是 「 阿拉伯語 」 、 「 kigai 」 、 「 kigai 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	在你生命中 , 生命中最危險的一年是生生的 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們活躍了 , 他們活躍了 , 他們活躍了他們的生活 , 值得大約七年的壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點點 , 而不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們吃肉 , 不是吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和甜蜜 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 能從桌子上擺脫 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接下來的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放到第一 , 照顧孩子和老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於一個信仰的社群 , 值得花四個時間 , 假如你花了四年的時間 , 預期壽命只有四倍 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生生 , 或他們正常被賦予 , 以適當的人為主 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從micham研究中學到 , 如果你三位最好的朋友都肥胖了 , 你就會有更好的機會 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人交流 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你的朋友喝了一個小東西 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝酒 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但沒有太多 , 他們都很投入 , 而且他們很有信任 , 而且他們很信任 , 而且他們很有信任 , 並且信任 , 那將會是實體活動 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食在歷史上沒有任何飲食 , 全世界的人口數量超過百分之二 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常在一月開始 , 通常是十月份 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	到長壽時 , 沒有短暫的治療 , 不用藥丸或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你思考一下 , 你的朋友是長期冒險的旅程 , 你的朋友是長期冒險的旅程 。 謝謝你 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	基礎上 , 卡塔里娜•莫塔里娜莫塔說: 「 要花點時間來玩 ! 卡塔里娜•莫塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔說: 「 時間 , 要玩這個東西 , 讓音樂有趣 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔里娜•莫塔里娜莫塔說: 「 要花點時間來玩耍 , 讓它有趣 。 」
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙 , 他的祖父建造了一輛車子 , 用腳踏車和洗衣機來運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這樣做 , 因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間 , 我們了解事情如何運作 , 以及它們如何運作 , 所以我們可以建造、修復它們 , 或至少能做出明確的決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀 , 許多這些人在20世紀時就失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社區和開放原始碼的模型就是把這些知識帶到他們面前的過程中 , 然後我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 來處理這些東西是如何運作的 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部份 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料像是紙和紡織物是如何製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人的可行性 , 顏色的塑膠 , 製造電力的塑膠 , 顏色的塑膠 , 會改變顏色 , 製造電力 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	電電電路板可以用傳統印刷電路或電路板或電路板
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個例子中 , 我們用它來製造一個觸摸感應器 , 用它來製造觸感感應器 , 用它來製造觸感感應器 , 用它來製造觸感感應器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	過去的藝術家最近發展出了 , 但最近的開發指出 , 我們很快就能夠用在雷射印表機和筆中 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張圖片是由無色的光譜組成的粒子組成的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 當一般的光線繞過整個表面的光線時 , 我會把光線轉換成光線 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料包含了內在設計和多觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	在溫度上 , 溫度會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個溫度的溫度上 , 只能稍微高一點一點 , 不像你能看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒瓶子裡 , 要讓內容很酷 , 可以喝酒 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以 , 這些只是少數人被稱為智慧材料的原料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會在日常生活中的許多物品和技術上使用 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行的汽車科幻小說 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度、鍵盤、旋轉 , 並且窗戶會轉變為光線 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 為什麼我今天要談的是智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是一個製造者 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇他們如何做 , 以及它們如何運作 , 但也因為我相信我們應該更深入了解它的組成 , 如何製造出我們的世界 , 而現在 , 我們並不知道這些高科技的複製品是如何運作的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的物質在小量中很難取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用來使用它們 , 很少有人說它們是如何生產的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們大部分在交易秘密和專利上 , 只有大學和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 凱西•男孩和我開始了一個專案 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是個網站 , 每個人都想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 發表信息 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 ,
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會希望它成為一個大型集體的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料來製造資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 我們為什麼要在乎智能的材料 , 以及他們所做的是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 , 以及我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們所穿的衣服 , 我們所使用的衣服 , 我們
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個充滿智慧型材料的世界 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 更重要的是 , 創新總是被吸引者 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 演員、個人電腦、飛機 , 都不是專家 , 而是從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學很複雜 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但 , 並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	在伊利諾州大學的兩個科學家 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用簡單的方法來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他從未經歷過化學 , 直到之後 , 閱讀這篇文章 , 用它的材料和工具來做實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一個烤箱 , 甚至製作了自己的創作者 , 他甚至製作了自己的創作 , 甚至是他自己創作的 , 甚至是他自己創作的 , 甚至是由另一個科學家/maker所製作的 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jordan在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的結果 , 甚至沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以jordan主要的創新方式就是在一個小型的實驗室裡做實驗 , 在芝加哥使用便宜材料和工具 , 讓他自己做到 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這份工作 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以挑選他出版的作品 , 其他人可以選擇他出版的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我要提倡她的專案計畫目標是要提高專注力和技能的創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 教導我們如何運作 , 但他們教導我們如何運作 , 和他們教導我們如何運作時 , 他們教導我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的另一方面 , 就是建立了一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常物品的工具 , 用來創造出不尋常物品的工具 , 用來創造出不尋常物品的工具 , 用來創造出不尋常的物件 , 以讓我們從前所未知的事物中 , 以創造出不尋常的物體 , 以讓我們從前所未知的事物
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的其中之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一塊紙 , 上面有一些銅板 , 它和一個磁鐵相連 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	因此 , 根據研究 , 漢娜的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的文件 , 用簡單的銅銅板來製造出一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅銅板來製造 , 來製造一系列的紙 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和其他作家一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的論文 , 讓任何人都能複製並繁殖他們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學的一部分 , 它允許我們創造便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的作品 , 和她分享她的發現 , 開啟了一系列的新可能性 , 包括美感和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	有趣的是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方法來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 越好的機會 , 我們就能創造出科技 , 才能真正保存我們 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代初期所做的 , 他寫道: 「 你必須理解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主題 , 只有科學家關心 , 而沒有任何夢想在家裡都可以做 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 保持在未來的知識新興技術是最好的方法 , 來確保我們有所謂的新興科技 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 讓每個人在路上行駛 。 但如果車子能與我們分享資料 , 將它們的速度和平衡 , 再加上我們 , 但如果車子能與我們分享資料 , 將它們的速度和速度相互相互 , 來計算安全的路線 , 讓每個人都在路上 , 不意外地發生了什麼 ?
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jeniferhealey:如果車子可以說話意外 , 意外可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來面對:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不想這樣做 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和幸運的事實 , 是我們不喜歡去思考的 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和幸運的地板在世界各地的地板讓我們知道這是真實的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國造成死亡的原因 , 75%的死亡率和百分之七十五的死亡率沒有任何藥品或酒精 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能確保 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是一位年輕的駕駛員 , 在我面前看到布拉克燈光 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢慢 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止 , 死停 , 停止死亡停止 , 停止死亡停止 , 停止死亡停止 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	僅僅是65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我打開車子 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停止 , 空氣袋的爆炸 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子也不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 我知道它不會停止 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子也停止了 。 我知道它不會停止 ,
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變開車的經驗 , 讓車子互相溝通 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們稍微了解駕駛現在的樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受到你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是 , 在超human的速度上 , 在超人速的速度上 , 超human的速度是很大的 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你需要指導你是兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 所以 , 所有你在做的事 , 都不是設計這個任務 , 但人們要求你做些什麼 , 你要做些什麼 , 首先他們要做些什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放在道路上 , 這是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看著你在哪裡 , 走路走路 , 不要看你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你們和其他人 , 這是安全的方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要做呢 ? 因為我們必須做 , 我們必須做出選擇 , 看看這裡嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾 , 我們錯了一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得錯了 , 或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數個意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒有看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在可以幫助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 我們將能夠看見這些車子 , 不只三輛車 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛觀看 , 我們將能夠看到這些車輛 , 同時 , 車子 , 和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們可以看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能看到在我們面前的車輛 , 看到車子的速度是多快的 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙在0 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維空間的物體 , 它有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路上行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在公路上發佈道路 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做理想的預測 , 對於車子在未來的情況下是很困難的 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車上 , 摩托車和摩托車 , 摩托車和摩托車騎士走了一小時 , 一小時下降了 , 我知道你有過這個經驗 , 不是 「 只是從哪裡來 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人已經在路上半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英里回來 , 有人看過這個人 , 他在地圖上 , 很快地圖上 , 看到那個傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上 , 很快地 , 他就在地圖上 , 地圖上 , 很快地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 很快地 , 他就在地圖上 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳朵中看到: 「 五分鐘、摩托車、摩托車、摩托車 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測 , 像是汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我是說 , 它們是牛頓物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們該怎麼辦到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 只要分享我們在車子之間的資料 , 分享我們的位置 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機在我的車裡 , 我有一個很精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我有非常精確的點子 , 我有非常精確的點子 , 我有很精確的點
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	用電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子 , 和他們在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車子一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的點子 , 和其他車子的概念相似 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車子分享資料 , 如果他們互相溝通 , 會如何 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬測驗結果 , 當車輛共享gps時 , 我們將這項研究應用在電腦模擬器上 , 當汽車共享gps時 , 我們將這個研究應用在電腦模擬器上 , 例如:鋼索攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬測驗 , 即便是用電腦模擬器 , 就可以在電腦模擬測驗中 , 即便是用電腦模擬器 , 而我們已經把這兩種視覺感應器放在電腦模擬器上 , 例如:鋼琴攝影機、gps , 和電腦模擬測驗 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也用了很短的距離頻道來溝通電線 , 機器人和彼此溝通 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相競爭時 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 牠們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們把更多的機器人加入混合物中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太過時 , 很難處理所有的包包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 所以你必須優先考慮 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人卡車正追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先考慮到一個人 , 看起來有點不好 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他是怎麼回事 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道駕駛你需要什麼駕駛才能避免 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是如何讓每個人成為最好的 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子的意思是: 「 你需要從路上走出來嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:一個 , 汽車的能力 , 第二位駕駛員的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在電話上 , 或你知道 , 做一些事情 , 他們不可能會在緊急狀態中最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	因此 , 我們開始了一系列的研究做司機狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們能偵測到 , 如果駕駛者往前走 , 看著手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們能預測出誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 可以預測誰 , 車子是最好的位置 , 來計算安全的安全路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術已經存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為最大的問題是 , 我們要分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個很不舒服的概念 , 這想法就是我們會把車子轉向另一輛車 , 我們會看著我們 , 和其他車子聊天 , 我們會在海中走路 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車從外面來 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的清單牌數字 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後說話 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位想像一下 , 如果你真的不希望你被告知你會死去 , 會死去 , 停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的數據 , 我們可以做到對每個人而言最好的 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來看看你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。

business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	企業、飛行、科學、短談、空間、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandis在史蒂芬•霍金 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我很熱衷於打開這個空間前面 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會讓世界專家在重力的重力中 , 這真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他透過archonxprize基因組學研究 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們競爭的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 第一組 , 將人類基因組排列在10天內 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們稱之為 「 基因組1000個個體 」 , 我們稱之為 「 基因組 」 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡爾斯•凡爾斯 。

and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到這裡 , 但我可以把你帶到零g 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	然後他說: 「 絕對是 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一一種方式就是 , 飛行器 , 無限飛行 , 無限飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一架飛機 , 飛過最高 , 你就無需25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再回來 , 重量兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	再一次 , 再一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你能得到8、10分鐘的無重度 , 太空總署的訓練是太空人如何訓練的 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	花了我們11年才才成為營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布我們要飛行史蒂芬霍金 。

and he wanted to go .	他想去了 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力得到所有許可 。

we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一個媒體會議 , 我們宣佈我們的內容是要給他25秒的0g 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的很好 , 我們可能會做3個癱瘓 。

i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想要鼓勵公共利益 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到肯定的太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的車中 , 進入太空中心 , 進入太空中心 , 進入太空中心 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐贈給兒童慈善團體的慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedsters 。

we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩個護士坐在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監控他的血壓 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們全都在緊急情況下 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界的專家 。

and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在剛剛的第一場爆炸之後 , 他微笑了 , 我們說 , 一切都很好 。 他笑了 , 我們說了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個癱瘓 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實會把一個蘋果帶到saac牛頓 , 因為教授霍金在劍橋大學的同一個椅子上發現了 , 艾薩克•牛頓是這樣 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第第四個 , 第五個第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七個和八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像65歲輪椅的輪椅 。

we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的猶太人 , 我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶中 , 在我們的生命中 , 我們正在移動這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這次的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫師戴維德•鮑林斯基y展示了三分鐘的刺激 , 顯示在細胞內的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•鮑林斯基y動畫了細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從一個不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	從我長大後 , 真相和美麗在科學中 , 真相和美麗的表達 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很美好的事物 , 但它們的真相和美麗 , 能夠被科學和數學所包圍 , 即使是科學家想要約會的熱情 , 都很美好 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真實的表達方式 , 意思是 , 說他們是你能做的事 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是很有力的 , 很有力的 , 很不可思議 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的 , 有時通常是很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你們可以從螢幕上看 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗是常常在科學中被誤解的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是用一種方式來描述美麗的事物 , 尤其是當你了解語言和文字時 , 那些研究主題的人 , 真正和美麗的事物是可以用的 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , 平方 , 如你所見 , 在宇宙中 , 數學是平等的 , 如果你觀察宇宙的理論 , 就會發現生命必須從數字來描述宇宙的觀點 , 這樣是很困難的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導時 , 我是被教導的 , 透過使用影像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用影像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過使用影像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由透過使用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由透過使用影像來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 藉由利用動畫來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生們常常在環境中被教導 , 他們學到的是真相和美麗並不總是有證據 , 但他們被教導的事物是有真相和美麗的 , 並不是總是有證據的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這幾乎就像是古老的食用雞 , 把雞肉黏在香味上 , 直到香味就消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣做對我們的學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以 , 我們有機會去真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學博士學院的電話叫robertlue在哈佛大學的一間電話中 , 他問我我團隊是否有興趣 , 且要真正改變醫學和科學教育是如何運作的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	因此 , 我們開始探索一個專案 , 讓學生可以理解更大的圖片 , 可以理解大型圖片 , 可以讓學生可以了解更大的圖片 , 可以了解它們能在哪裡找到的真相和美麗 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以擁有一個顯微複雜的城市 , 一個大型複雜的城市 , 由微生物組成 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微型機制 , 是由胺基酸所製造出來的 , 具有強大、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精準、精確的裝置 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微微m細胞運動如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能發揮作用力 。 它們能發揮我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	她們的力量是我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 把這些視野化的觀點放在腦海裡 , 讓這些學生能夠找到真正的生物觀點 , 像是哈佛大學的生物觀點 , 像是哈佛大學的研究 , 像是哈佛大學的生物學學生 , 他們的圖像會被激發出來 , 這樣他們就可以研究這個觀點 , 想像一下 , 真的 , 生命是如何運作的 , 這樣他們才能找到真正的 , 生命的運作方式 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子如何組合在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們做了一個主題 , 這裡有一種發炎熱血管的細胞 , 裡面有噴射器的細胞 , 它們在附近的細胞壁上 , 它們會接觸到外表的細胞 , 它們會吸收到細胞壁上的資訊 , 它們會接觸到細胞外面的細胞 , 它們會吸收到細胞壁上的資訊 , 它們會觸碰到外面的細胞 , 它們會吸收到細胞壁上的資訊 。

so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子分子馬達我們必須與哈佛科學家和研究者合作 , 找出它們如何移動 , 並找出它們是如何移動的 。

and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是 , 一個3分鐘的閱讀者的消化版本 , 這是我們製作的第一個面向 , 它是一部關於我們製作的電影的第一面 , 它是一個持續進步的計畫 , 可以到另外四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看到這些小行走的路徑 , 它們叫做 「 金絲 」 , 用這些巨大的道路來處理這些巨大的道路 , 它們會挑戰螞蟻的距離 。
run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內運作得非常驚人 , 它們其實是生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都能與彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們通過資訊傳遞訊息 。

and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出這些部分 , 從資訊中從原子核的分子中取代 , 從資訊傳送到基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	從最小的生命到每一個人 , 都沒有這些小小的生命 , 沒有這些小小的微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器中 , 克里斯 , 真的 , 很不可思議 , 克里斯 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex的dart細胞 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他採取了一堆新的製造蛋白質 , 包含所有品牌新的製造蛋白質 , 不管它是否需要在細胞中 , 或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西正在運作 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你覺得多麼瘋狂 , 你其實沒有什麼 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當我回家想想看 , 我們的大腦有多強大 。

but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但真的很驚人 , 這些細胞 , 細胞需要這些細胞 , 才知道這些細胞的需求 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做得做的事 。
