becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅館去年 , 看到國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的婚姻在她的旅程結束時 , 她的經歷變成了無家可歸的一份子 , 讓她成為一個美國無家可歸的年輕人 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會變遷、社會、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪.布朗頓:那年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家、記者、記者 , 我知道如何做很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到要做的事情之一就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了無家可歸的一員 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職了一份報紙編輯 , 決定要去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的命令我很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	有許多事情我想要感覺和處理我在做的事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我把整個人生都放進去了 , 我決定住在一個旅行的旅行中 , 一趟旅行是一趟旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 我的輪椅和我的車子 , 開了1975年的火車 , 開車到日子 , 完全失敗了 , 發現了三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平均生活在永久的結構中 , 甚至是一堆 , 一個人的價值觀 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 了解到別人對別人的負面感知如何影響我們的現實 , 如果我們能做到 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失敗地意識到無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 生活在火車上 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡 , 常常打開 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱 , 是我父親的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我必須得到一份全職的工作 , 來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時 , 一個非常熱的夏天夏天會變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到公園裡 , 沒有很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和狗狗 , 非常熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過了開窗的窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	那個狗花了好幾天 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能使用員工 , 卡車站在辦公室裡 , 卡車就停止了 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共場合裡發聲 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度降到80度以上 , 華氏80度的溫度下降到華氏80度 , 讓它很難或不可能睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐蝕 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰層的冰層上升了三分之一 , 這很糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起一間公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 , 不負擔得起一間公寓 , 不能負擔得起公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們放棄 , 所以我留在火車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱讓我太生病時 , 我用了一桶汽油桶 , 用一桶汽油桶 , 用一桶汽油桶 , 用一桶汽油桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣溫下降時 , 溫度下降了 , 溫度下降了 , 溫度下降了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停下來 , 所以我會避免注意到 , 被警察攔截 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我人生的掌控 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道 , 但那是如何發生的 , 我不知道它是怎麼發生的 , 但是我從一位有名的作家和記者 , 變成了無家可歸的家人 , 一名無家可歸的女性 , 直到無家可歸的家人 , 帶著我的呼吸走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商 , 沒有變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 所有我都不一樣的東西 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我送到一個無家可歸的醫療診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我走了 , 三天內就沒有洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我身為一個人 , 身為一個人 , 和憂鬱症患者一樣 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾位無家可歸的人發現 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 , 你是不是無家可歸的 , 他們說: 「 你是無家可歸的 。 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的家人 , 但我也沒見過 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	無家可歸的無家可歸 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥物給了我的憂鬱症 。 我記得在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 沒有人會注意到 。
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 不久後 , 她聽說過湯姆•魯斯特 , 一個全國性的記者 , 一直在談論我 , 全國的新聞報導 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇文章 , 是在提姆的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , 主題是 「 會議 」 的主題時 , 我開始笑話 , 當時我住在一個沃爾瑪的公園大廳裡 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑聲 , 因為那時候 , 我是作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的女性 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 把我的論文寫下來 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬到田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我生活在一個旅館裡 , 和朋友交流 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	今年夏天 , 我是個記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎勵 , 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再看不見了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人全職工作 , 生活在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續犯罪 , 或在街道上 , 或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一群人 , 他們鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 鼓勵他們 ,
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何東西 , 如果有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是在這裡 , 要是無家可歸的女士 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是在這裡鼓勵你去鼓勵你去鼓勵你 , 去鼓勵你去鼓勵你 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位的是 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個沃爾瑪的火車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , thailand " sthailand " sthailand " sthailand " 的先步:人口控制 。 這意味著 , 很多frank , thailand " mr. " 的 " dom "mechange , thailand " mr. " 。 意思是 , 很多frank , change , thailand " dom " 。 意思是 , 我們有了許多的法蘭克 , 非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	伊維拉維拉維拉瓦達: 「 怎麼做泰國更好的情況 。 」
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	當我在貧窮時 , 一個二十年前 , 國家非常非常貧窮 , 許多人生活在貧窮 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從一個福利計畫或貧窮的案件開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭的計畫開始 , 有一個非常成功的兒童健康活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人接受家庭計劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:讓孩子們接觸到媽媽 , 然後追隨家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我帶各位回到我們為什麼要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	7個小孩 , 每家人的成長率高達3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女子說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來阻止藥丸 。 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來打噴藥 。 」
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有得到答案 , 我們不把問題當作 。

author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者 , 當然 , 熱情在這個演說中 , 創意了女性主義的定義 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球性議題、愛、父母、故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿拉伯爾都說出了熱情的熱情 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	謝謝各位 。 非常可怕的是 , 這裡是非常可怕的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴各位一些關於熱情的熱情 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相呢 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事者 , 我想要說出比真相更真實的事實 , 是我們共同的人類 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我有興趣 , 直到我最後寫了它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些人會繼續下去:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的神秘 , 所以我寫了關於巧合、情緒、夢想、魔法的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去20年 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但在2006年 , 當我在義大利的奧林匹克市旗下 , 參加奧林匹克市旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這使我成為了名人 。 現在人們認出我是很酷的 , 和孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們關於我四分鐘的信息 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克法典禮儀的其中一位參選者 , 叫做我 , 說我被選為是旗幟之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答這問題 , 是因為我身分是個運動員 , 因為你能從運動員身上得到運動員 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在場地上游泳 , 甚至不確定我可以走到水中去 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑聲 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 唯一女性會帶著奧林匹克旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女性 , 代表五個大陸 , 還有三位奧林匹克贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 天然 , 天然我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個制服 , 她說 , 請求我的測量 。

by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	在二月時 , 我發現我自己在街頭 , 熱情感激的群眾 , 每八十個奧林匹克都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員已經犧牲了一切在遊戲中競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應該要贏 , 但有幸運的運算 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一片冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定結果 , 或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心臟就會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	重點是熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其覆蓋著紅色海報 , 宣佈了奧林匹克的圖表 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在此 , 不是總是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心臟是驅動我們並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中所需要的角色:熱情心臟 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要大師、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者、外叛者 ,
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	很有意思的人 , 不會有創意的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	牠們只會做好前的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在溫室 , 我遇見了其他旗幟:三項運動員 , 和蘇菲亞•洛倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	另外 , 兩位女士有熱情心臟:wangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她改變了土壤、氣候、天氣 , 在某些地方 , 在非洲的其他地方 , 並且在許多村落裡進行了 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	瑪麗媽媽 , 一位柬埔寨活動家 , 他對抗孩童機構有熱情的抗議 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	十四歲時 , 她的祖父賣了她到哥哥 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們小女孩被男人強暴 , 那些相信性愛的人 , 會幫助他們愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們被迫接收到五、十五個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們會被強迫接收到五個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們會被強迫接受五個客戶 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我接受了我的制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我所預期的 , 不是壞事 , 真的 , 真的 。 不錯 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟都是美麗和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲亞在七十歲時 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她是性愛、脆弱、和高塔 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深度的坦尚和沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪問時問: 「 她怎麼能看得好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我不讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你有一些自由建議 , 來自世界上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒人 , 不打招呼 , 沒有打招呼 , 沒有煩惱 , 沒有打擊 , 沒有打擊 , 沒有打擊 , 沒有打擊 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她不這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	晚上 , 我們在午夜的時候 , 我們被告示了奧林匹克旗 , 音樂也開始了 , 奧林匹克市旗幟演出 , 音樂也開始了 , 奧林匹克旗 , 音樂也開始了 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲亞•洛倫在我面前面前 , 比我還高 , 不在我面前 , 她是腳塔比我 , 還不算出口頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她走廊時 , 穿著旗幟 , 穿著衣服的旗幟 , 直到她肩膀上 , 拿著旗子的旗幟 , 直到她肩膀上 , 把旗幟綁在她的肩膀上 , 所以我的頭其實是一支旗子 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的攝影機都在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我常常在索菲亞的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分的人都喜歡這個地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我整個人生中最好的四分鐘 , 就是在奧林匹克運動場 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我跟他說 , 儘管我告訴他 , 我們在私人身上做的事 , 通常只有4分鐘 , 但他不應該這樣做 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個美好的消息 , 因為我不想忘記他們當老年齡毀了我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我希望在我心中 , 奧運的關鍵字是 「 奧林匹克熱情 」 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡是熱情的熱情 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	那年是1998年 , 這個地方是一個監獄營地 , 位置在剛果的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和殘疾人士都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為 「 死亡營地 」 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人 , 會被殺死 , 或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅斯地圖和她的小孩 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她看著她的丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼 , 她會讓她的七個孩子活下來 , 幾個月後 , 她給出生出生殖雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她把黏液黏在黏土上 , 並用她的頭髮做結尾 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她稱之為雙胞胎 , 用黑茶茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法保持他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵把槍擊到她的頭上 , 她抓住了她 , 抓住她 , 抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 , 她抓住她 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎樣 , 這家生存活了十六個月 , 很幸運 , 美國人的熱情心臟 , 亞利桑那州 , 亞利桑那州 , 讓她有美麗的心情 , 一位年輕美國人的心情 , 亞利桑那州 , 讓她成為美國人的心臟 , 亞利桑那州 , 讓她成為美國人的熱情心 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖西里 , 在波希里 , 意思是很棒的愛情 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書籍的主張都很強烈和熱情的女性 , 比如羅斯•地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會把它們放進去 , 沒有需要 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我看著周圍 , 看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和女性和女人一起工作 , 為女性和我的生活 。
i know them well .	我知道他們很好 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古老的時期 , 在世界各地 , 在一個父權和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 五歲時 , 我是一位女權主義者雖然沒有達到智利 , 但沒人知道問題是什麼 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 有一個高價錢可以付出我的自由 , 去為我解決問題 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出這一切 , 因為每一塊我收到的每一塊 , 我都能得到兩份 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦 , 當我女兒保羅拉在她的二十歲時 , 她告訴我 , 女權主義是約會的 , 我應該搬進去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了不可思議的戰鬥 , 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 如今我女兒和所有我們今天的女性 , 但對我們大部分的妹妹們來說 , 不論是誰 , 還是強迫勞動力勞工 , 她們有孩子 , 她們不想要或她們無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被強暴 , 有時被殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分西方的年輕女性主義者是個侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性別過 , 但讓我保證 , 我從來沒有過過性感 , 讓我保證她從來沒有過過性感 , 讓我保證從來沒有過過性感 , 讓我保證她從來沒有過過性感 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義不是死 , 沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 給上帝的命運 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 " 愛滋病 " 或 " 愛滋病 " 或 " 不管 " 的名字 , 不論你想要什麼 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們也支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉的一個村落裡 , 有一個小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國牙醫牙醫師 , 在她的三週假期 , 要去診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒 , 但當她走到那裡 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一群女性 , 等待了幾小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位患者是非常痛苦的因為她有幾種羅特的媽媽
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一的解決方法就是去除掉壞牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有做過這種事 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適合的儀器 , 但幸運的是她已經帶了一些鼻子 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇氣和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她向禱告祈禱 , 她向前邁進 , 帶著行動 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生醫師推出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 她的第一個病人在等待她的丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像水龍 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是非常腫脹的 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮害怕她做了什麼事 , 但後來翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術沒有關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	第一天 , 她的丈夫打敗她 , 因為她沒有家來準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬的女性住在像這樣 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	儘管女性有三分之二的勞動力 , 但世界各地的勞動力只有不到1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性一樣工作 , 只要他們付錢 , 他們就被剝削、暴力虐待、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 提供女性教育、工作 , 和自己的能力 , 來控制自己的收入、遺產、以及自己的財產 , 來控制自己的收入、遺產、以及自己的財產 , 來控制自己的收入、遺產、以及自己的收入 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女性有權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家 , 最終都能完成整個國家 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai在肯亞的村落 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 說 , 土地是荒野的 , 因為他們砍掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女去植物新的樹木和水 , 滴滴 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年間 , 他們有森林砍伐 , 土壤被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最最貧窮的最貧窮最貧窮最最窮最最窮最最貧窮的社會總是把女性放進去 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但顯然的事實是忽略政府和慈善事業 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給男性的計畫 , 二十美金給男性的計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們能改變一切 , 不只是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證各位 , 女性一起工作 , 結合起來 , 受教育 , 和平與繁榮 , 能夠讓大家一起連結 , 知識和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的戰爭中 , 大部分的戰爭都是公民 , 主要是女性和小孩 , 主要是婦女和小孩 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人在問的問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	是否合理參與這個世界秩序 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生命的品質是為每個人 , 不僅僅是為了榮幸 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月 , 我看到了費倫多•布萊圖書館的畫作 , 圖書館的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或ghraib監獄 , 除了紐約ghraib監獄的作品中 , 都沒有博物館或藝術家 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的痛苦和虐待的力量 , 在大型的畫作中 , 暴風雨 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法從我的心中得到這些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我害怕大部分的力量是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 而權力濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則改變了所有時間 , 但他們總是會得到益處 , 在這個案例中 , 失敗的效果 , 並不是在經濟上運作 , 很完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	下層的層面下降到底層 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩子 , 特別是貧窮 , 特別是貧窮 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最多的女人還是小孩 , 他們都能虐待女性或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我在許多性別、收入、種族和課堂上都有能力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間在文明中創造基礎的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要女性能源在世界各地 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要培養女性權力的女性權力而我們需要培養女性的女性權力
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我在談的是男性 , 當然 , 當然 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老舊人無希望 ; 我們等待他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很喜歡有蘇菲亞•洛倫的長腿和腿部和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了選擇 , 我寧願是瑪麗•瑪麗的母親 , 珍妮 , 和羅斯地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 但要讓它好好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為何不呢 ? 它可能存在 。 在這個房間裡所有的知識、能源、天才和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來吃飯 , 把我們的粉絲帶進去 , 創造出一個完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每一天 , 在城市裡 , 大小的倫敦、三千萬美金的餐廳 , 但那裡的食物來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡羅倫敦 , 設計了一座城市 , 展示了古代的食物如何形成現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史蒂爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵食一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	然而 , 卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們很理想地說 , 如果去了一間餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 到一間餐廳 , 到處都是餐廳 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到每一天 , 城市都要被運輸、買賣、煮飯、吃、被摧毀 , 或被製造出來 , 被賣掉、吃掉、被摧毀 , 就像倫敦的城市一樣 , 必須要被製造出來 , 被運輸、買賣、煮飯、吃掉 , 和其他東西一樣 , 只要在地球上發生 , 一切都很糟糕 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這個地方 , 就像人類古老的祖先一樣 , 我們依賴自然世界 , 以我們的古老祖先生存 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們搬進城市裡 , 更多的自然世界都被轉變為非凡的景色 , 像是我在巴西的田野 , 來餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的地景 , 但少數人看到他們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景並不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	越來越多人正在吃肉 , 所以 , 現今的三分之一的穀物被餵食給動物 , 而不是給人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	若要用三倍的穀物來餵養人類 , 那就不是很有效的方法 , 可以餵飽人類 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個很嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 它估計了我們將要活在城市裡的人口數量 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時也估計有兩倍肉和大量肉都被消耗掉 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉和城市主義都在手上 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這會造成一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億個飢餓的牛肉 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個很大的問題 。 事實上如果我們把我們帶到這一步 , 我們就很難解決這個問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的雨林 , 都失去了 , 創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同樣的時間 , 我們失去了同一等量量的儲存量 , 以致於氣候變遷 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也很渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	花了大約10卡路里 , 來生產我們所消耗的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有食物在大成本上 , 我們並不珍視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半的食物被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這段漫長過程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有辦法讓地球適合 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們有十億人是肥胖者 , 一十億人是肥胖 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為百分之八十的全球貿易已經被五個跨國企業所控制 , 它是一張圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬進城市時 , 世界也擁抱了西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是一個不可持續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼走到這裡的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答一些簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這是在古老的早期 , 叫做 「 肥沃克里斯 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是具體的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這兩個非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是個意外 , 因為農業和城市都互相合作 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它是從古老祖先的祖先開始產生的食物來源足夠穩固地維持永久居住環境
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些居住的環境 , 我們看到它們是比較的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被大型寺廟包圍著 , 中央食物分配中心 , 食物分配中心的食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是神聖的神殿 , 把穀物取代 , 把穀物給上帝 , 再把食物帶給神 , 再給上帝 , 再給上帝們 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 整個精神和實體生活都是由穀物和穀物所組成的 , 這些城市的主要是由穀物及收藏所組成的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都一樣 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有的都是小小的 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名的 , 羅馬有大約一百萬個公民 , 位於第一世紀的廣告 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼 , 這種城市如何像這樣養活自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物英哩 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬接觸了海洋 , 讓它可以從遠遠的路上取得海洋 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一能做到的辦法 , 因為它很難運輸食物 , 路邊是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然是很快的 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬效應的戰役 , 像是卡和埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 擴張帝國的擴張 , 其實是很長的一段漫畫 , 包含了軍事化購物中心 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我真的很喜歡這個事實:羅馬事實上 , 我很喜歡這句話:羅馬其實是從倫敦來到倫敦的一個階段 , 我覺得這很奇特 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形狀它的形狀 , 羅馬形塑了它的地形 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦的地圖的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的地圖是從十七世紀開始的地圖 , 它的地圖是來自葉子的地圖 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 黃金市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們到便宜的道路 , 主要市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看這條街頭的名字 , 你可以告訴你在300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚類也來自河流 , 也是一樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 很有名的說法是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這很不尋常 , 當你想到它的時候 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人都在移動電話裡 , 看起來像磚塊 , 像磚塊一樣 , 像磚塊一樣 , 像磚塊一樣 , 像磚塊一樣 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一種食物在城市裡的食物:一旦它根入城市中 , 它們非常稀少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是一種非常不同的故事因為當然 , 動物可以走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	很多倫敦的肉來自於蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 它來到那裡 , 到達北部的西北部 , 這是為什麼smithfield , 倫敦是史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦是史密菲爾德 , 非常有名的肉市場 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	來自東加利亞 , 到東部 , 到東部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女性 , 這樣做 , 鳥兒們來到他們的腳邊 , 用雙腳來保護小小的玻璃 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們抵達東方時 , 被賣掉的地方就是他們所謂的 「 多數 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看在工業時代的地圖 , 你能從工業時代取得食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何塑造食物的 , 藉由閱讀街道的名字 , 讓你們知道它是如何形狀的 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街道 , 在一個星期五的街道上 , 你去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你必須想像一下它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間就是食物被買賣的唯一地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看史密斯密斯密斯密斯密斯密斯密斯密斯密斯密度的圖像 , 你可以看到在1830年時 , 它會很難生活在這個城市裡 , 不管你從哪裡得到食物 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有陽日午餐 , 機會是在你的窗戶外面 , 或在你的窗戶外面五天前走出你的窗戶 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很顯然是一個有機的城市 , 一部分是有機循環 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西方的圖片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你們可以看到 , 有些最早的訓練乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被屠殺了 , 不論是在國內的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	後來他們進入城市裡 , 被鐵帶回來 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 要開始發展城市 , 真的可以在任何地方都能做到 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市以前被地理所限制 , 他們習慣要把食物帶到非常困難的實體上 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們被解放了地理學 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的地圖上 , 到九十年後 , 在火車之後 , 它會變成一個大型的蜘蛛 , 要餵飽足夠的動物 , 很容易被動物送進去 , 所以 , 不管是哪種 , 都很容易被動物吃掉 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是一開始 , 火車才剛剛開始 。 火車結束了這個過程 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是整個城市的最後一個與大自然的聯繫 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市 , 沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景下走動 , 沒有人會夢想著那樣的走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們買了食物 , 拿到箱子裡 , 拿到箱子裡的一週 , 買到箱子裡 , 想出了什麼 , 去做些什麼 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是我們的關係 , 食物和城市 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 該城市的核心位置 , 該城市的核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們習慣烹飪 ; 現在我們只是加入水 , 或一些蛋糕的蛋糕 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物來看看是否好吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛剛就讀了一包背後的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們沒有價值食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 我們將它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統最棒的諷刺之一就是他們做了一件很棒的諷刺 , 就是他們做得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由創造城市 , 任何地方 , 都能在我們和大自然中建立起任何地方 , 將我們和大自然連結起來 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只要他們能做到 , 我們就看得到 , 不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯會問自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列的獨立建築物 , 像是一系列的獨立建築物 , 每人都很熟悉 , 一天會從另一邊走出 , 很熟悉的餐廳 , 吃飯後的菜園 , 和餐廳的餐廳 , 一起吃飯 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你可以說食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使從來沒有這麼說 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個非常有名的烏托邦 " 烏托邦 " 的名字: 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 烏托邦 」 、 「 烏托邦 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列獨立的城市 , 單獨的土地 , 加入了一輛獨立的城市 , 加入了另一條鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他的視野的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至建造了 , 但沒有用這種視覺去做 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的想法是烏托邦的想法 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾所使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有雙重的旋轉 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以說是好的 , 不論是哪個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個理想的 , 是我們無法做到的 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類的深層問題 , 會讓它不用用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 例如: 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 西班牙語 」 、 「 地點 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在烏托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在世界各地 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來形塑這個世界 , 而如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來形塑這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以 , 若我們要做 , 那會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我認為它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 看看狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	不管怎樣 , 這是食物在生活的中心 , 家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝 , 享受 , 人們花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	食物應該在我們的社會中 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能像這樣的景象 , 像這樣 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這些人也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 誰會想 , 誰會想食物 , 誰會想起食物 , 誰會想到食物 , 誰會想到食物呢 ?
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為 , 沒有這些我們無法擁有這樣的人 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我真的選了這個 , 因為這是一個人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 市場 , 食物正在成長的地方 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很常見 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是社會生活中的一部分 。

weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	幾週以來 , 卡爾斯蒂夫在21世紀 , 查爾斯壯觀看宗教的角色在21世紀:它會否認同情心 , 還是會把我們共同的好 ? 她重新審查了一百七十個禮物 , 來尋找宗教的角色在21世紀:它會把黃金法則給予我們嗎 ?
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenmstrong:讓我們重新審視黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我一直都很沮喪 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出自己的版本 , 叫做黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候 , 它會出現在正面的版本中: 「 總是對待你自己 , 讓其他人都等待你 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本: 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它是什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 都能讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 都能讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 都會造成痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調了同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它是好的 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們把黃金法定為 「 日常生活 」 和 「 日常生活 」 時 , 不只會做好事 , 然後回到人生中 , 和憤怒 , 反而是 , 直到今天 , 再回到一生中 , 更加深刻地 , 生活在你的世界中 , 然後再回到一個生活中 , 和憤怒 , 直到你說: 「 每天 , 一切都不會 。 」
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶到前所未有的名稱上帝、nirvana、rama、nirvana、rama
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不會知道很多時間 , 這才是宗教生活的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些奇妙的例外 , 當宗教信仰者聚集在一起 , 宗教團聚會聚集在一起 , 他們爭論辯論時 , 宗教團聚會聚在一起 , 他們會爭論 , 不論是宗教人聚在一起 , 宗教領袖一起聚在一起 , 他們會爭論說 , 宗教團聚在一起 , 宗教團聚在一起 , 他們對同性戀或對同性戀有興趣 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不想同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時候會看到 , 當我說到宗教人的同意時 , 會被視為是對的 , 是因為人們常常想要對抗 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然 , 這絕對是運動的目標 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感謝ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們把我帶到21世紀 , 把我帶到21世紀 , 讓我更廣泛的聽見 , 比我能想像的更廣泛 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	若我們不經營制定世界 , 無論他們是誰 , 或誰可能是誰 , 他們可能是誰 , 我懷疑我們有可行的工具 , 來對抗下一代的人 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們時間的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 人們可以一起生活和平 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而宗教應該要做主要的貢獻 , 而不是被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教信仰者相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的靈魂 , 想像性的同理心 , 把自己放到另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有選擇 , 對我而言 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	可以說: 「 這對你的鄰居是有意義的 , 不管你的鄰居是誰 , 當他站在一條腿上 , 說: 「 對你來說 , 這對你的鄰居是有意義的 。
