mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院學院學院的研究者 , 不是建造東西 , 我們能創造出材料 , 建立自己組合的結構 , 來建造一些東西 , 我們能創造出材料 , 建立自己組裝的結構 , 來建造一些東西 , 我們能創造出材料 , 它可以在自我組裝的構造中建立起來 , 可以在自我組裝的構造中 , 可以創造出它們 , 可以創造出它們的結構 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天際星球帽:我們能讓自己做些什麼嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我要向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築物和機器會自我組合 , 複製並修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向各位展示我相信目前的製造過程 , 然後將它與某些自然系統相比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業 , 我們有天花板 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 非常複雜、新的、令人興奮的技術 , 包括鋼筋、水泥、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有很興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年內 , 大約有250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 有兩百萬種種類 , 或dna , 或dna , 我們有兩百萬種類型 , 可以摺疊在大約一個小時內 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有許多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們很難犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	牠們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然體系有很有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把它轉換成我們的建設環境 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力 , 是我們建立的環境 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要在實體環境中使用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們所想要建立的複雜性 , 來建造我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要編寫程式的部分 , 可以採取那個序列 , 用它來摺疊或重複 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 使我們能用這個方案來摺疊程式 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些類型錯誤的反射線來保證我們成功地建立了我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些我和我同事的專案 , 麻省理工學院正在努力達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一兩個是麥克魯機器人和機器人 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計劃是大規模的可重視機器人 , 十二英尺 , 十二英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們用機械電子裝置 , 感測器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將你想要摺疊成一個序列的角度 , 轉換為120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120、120 , 等等 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都要把它送到鄰近 , 讓它負面120個路徑 , 把它送到附近 , 在那裡 , 然後把它送到鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是聰明的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師在這個計畫上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我覺得這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人為了製造這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否實現它嗎 ? 可以把機器人送進每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 通過性地 , 或熱情地嘗試修復程式設計 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會更進一步 , 試著用實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它基本上是計算數位邏輯 , 直接進入你的部位 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nandgate 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	這裡有兩個輸入鐵 , 裡面有兩個輸輸的通訊 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是使用者的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前面的磚塊被蓋出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	接著 , 它會給你一個輸入3d空間的空間 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊上做些什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算了它在做什麼 , 和你說你想要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , 1.1 , 輸入1.1 , 輸入中 , 輸入21.1 , 輸入中 , 就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0.0輸入是1輸入 , 它是1的輸出 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的信息都被建構出來了 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構含有藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入 , 告訴你如何解決這個問題 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些攀爬 , 閱讀它 , 並且可以輸入其中一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接被嵌入 , 沒有外外的指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	最後一個專案我稱之為 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 就是我們有自動自組系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重組和設計能力 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上 , 你有一連串元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每個鏈 , 或左派 , 都想要轉右或左右 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以 , 當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位 , 如果它應該轉右或左右 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成你在這個案件中所設計的任何組合 , 例如 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你基本上可以用三維空間的形狀或維度的形狀或維度 , 維持到這個鏈上完全被動地 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 我們的新可能性 , 可以自我組裝、複製、修復身體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分中有新的程式能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從你有新的可能性來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這很不可思議 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些項目是我剛剛展示的這些新的自我組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登陸了大陸 , 甚至在海洋中最深的一點點 。 下一代去探索生物學家和探索生物學家和探索者納森•沃爾夫提出答案:幾乎所有東西 , 我們都能開始 , 說 , 地球上最深的一點點 , 可能是地球上最深的一點點 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、生物多樣性、探索、微生物學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:我們要探究什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去拜訪了布萊斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那時候是很棒的二十世紀探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼和雷斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館裡 , 博物館長期以來未知的區域 , 如今 , 阿爾伯沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他真的是個人 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他就說 , 印度娜瓊斯特的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在布魯威斯康斯康斯康辛 , 我給一群中間學校學生提供了公共演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果有比在ted演講中有更嚇人的話 , 會試著把注意力集合成千上萬個12歲的小孩 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在課程結束時 , 他們問了一些問題 , 但那有一件事是真的困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該探索哪裡 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 在地球上有許多人都知道 , 在地球上 , 最深層的探索 , 就是為了要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到明顯的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但 , 真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們是否在地球上探索左邊的地球上沒有重要性 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我想到我最喜歡的探險家在生物學的研究中 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯•貝伊斯 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck發現了菸草疾病的結果 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是 , 他把感染的汁液從菸草植物中拿出來 , 用更小的濾器來過濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到這個點 , 知道細菌的生命中 , 最小的生命中 , 已經有所謂的細菌 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字 , 名為神秘的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露的病毒中 , 尼克真的開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒將基因信息傳播到地球上 , 遠超過所有其他生命組合的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 這種世界有很大的實際應用 , 像是消滅天花、疫苗的預防疫苗 , 我們現在知道 , 最主要是由人類prom病毒組成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck發現了 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百年前 , 蜜蜂鳥發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有自動飛行器 , 但我們沒意識到 , 地球上所有基因資訊的形式 , 造成了大部分的基因資訊 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	現在我們有了這些奇妙的工具讓我們能夠探索外面的世界 , 不僅僅是微生物群體的微生物群體 , 我們也能藉由這些物種的微生物群體來記錄所有遺傳訊息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以運用這些技術 , 從土壤到皮膚和所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在用一種規定的基準來判斷出爆發的疫情 , 無法阻止它們發生 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從每個人身上拿出一根口袋 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常用來尋找呼吸流感病毒的病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到的是巨大的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人的基因信息 , 包括細菌和病毒資訊 , 大部分是來自於你鼻子裡的任何東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會看到大約20%的基因信息在你鼻子裡 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於小組的研究 , 我們其實研究這些數據 , 其中一些人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生理學暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前所見過的東西 , 它和我們所見過的基因信息息息息息息息相關 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為20%的基因信息是生物暗物質 , 若我們觀察你的腸道 , 大約有40%或50%的基因信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質 , 無法被分類或配合我們所見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們以為這可能是工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度的序列工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假設解釋了生物暗物質的存在 , 只是在它們的生態暗物質中 , 但在這個生命中 , 有一個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:埋葬在這個生命中 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 存在著生命中 , 存在於這些遺傳信息中 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些弦 , 像是beijerinck , 基本上改變了我們對自然生物學的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許會讓我們找出癌症的原因 , 來找出癌症的原因 , 或找出我們不熟悉的新工具 , 或辨識出癌症的疾病 , 或找出我們所熟悉的疾病 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能告訴大家 , 在史丹佛大學和加州大學的同事們 , 我們現在正在開始一項探討生物暗物質 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 存在於生命的新形式 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們不了解病毒 , 生命的形式 , 使我們地球上大部分的基因信息息息相關 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到我們新階段的生命 , 可能完全不存在於我們的鼻子裡 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	是真的 , 我們可能在地球上發現所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示 , 地球上沒有任何東西可以去探索地球 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	貝洛威斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康斯康辛辛辛苦 , 為下一代的探險家提供了一個重要的課題 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們用這句話來做 , 像這樣:不要假設我們現在所認為的 , 就是這個故事:不假設我們現在認為的是什麼 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	不論你選擇去探索哪個領域 , 都能選擇去探索 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	不知我們周圍的事物 , 都等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	法律科學家大衛•迪普斯奇博士提出了理論物理 , 反覆思考更緊急的問題:地球暖化的理論物理 , 他說 , 要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷 , 氣候變遷 , 宇宙 , 文化 , 環境 , 全球問題 , 科學 , 科技 , 宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出來 , 說出令人意外的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 大家都知道的 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的紀錄歷史都已知名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	也就是說 , 地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或任何東西 , 都能維持我們的演化和創造力 , 以至於我們現在存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來存活 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今天 , 這個想法有一個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	此外 , 宇宙是外太空船 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 而我們所處的一切都依靠著 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們把太空船放進去 , 我們就沒辦法去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 所有人都知道 , 與人類歷史上相反 , 人類歷史上沒有 , 事實上 , 人類的存在 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球 , 在典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 在一個典型的星球上 , 它在一個典型的星球上 , 繞著一個典型的星球 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家知道的第二個說法是:我們在一個很典型的地方 , 第二個是說 , 我們在一個很典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩者視為深實的真相 , 將他們視為真相 , 然後他們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	第二個概念是:典型的 。 嗯 , 嗯 , 我們來看看一下 , 一個典型的空間:典型的嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們來看看一下 , 一個典型的空間 , 一個典型的空間 。 嗯 , 我們會看到牆壁 , 化學物質 , 不是典型的空間 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只能看到一顆藍色的行星 , 如果你遠遠超過一百英里 , 你會看到太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽、太陽 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星是星系 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	在宇宙中 , 大部分地方在宇宙中 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們進一步 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向外星系 , 向我們展示 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然處在宇宙中的一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須走到一千倍以外的地方 , 來到一個典型的地方 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ?典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的樣子是什麼 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在很大的期間 , ted已經排放了一個高解析度的虛擬實境空間 , 用高解析度的虛擬現實 , 來分析虛擬實境的空間 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們可以有燈光 , 請 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看到的空間是完全黑暗的 , 完全漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗的是 , 如果你要看著最近的恆星 , 看著你最接近的星球 , 你就會看到 , 直到那顆星星被撞擊 , 你仍然無法看見一個超新星 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的多大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此 , 一個超級新星很明亮 , 很明亮 , 所以很聰明的 , 很明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 非常明亮 , 如此
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星際空間中 , 遠遠遠離你看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	它也非常寒冷 , 不到三度 , 絕對零 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空氣 , 空氣比地球上最高的空氣有一百萬倍 。 所以 , 這裡有一百萬倍的密度 , 比我們最高的空氣中最高的真空 , 真空中 , 我們最高的真空可以創造出這個地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的樣貌 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們可以有燈光回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們如何知道一個環境是如此遙遠、外星 , 和我們所使用的環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球的環境 , 我們的形式是創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛剛提到的 , 我是指望遠鏡 , 你看到的東西看起來像星星一樣 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 水龍 」 , 原本的意思是 「 水龍 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著 , 看起來像星星一樣 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是數十億年前 , 數十億年前 , 數十億年前 , 星系中的物質在銀河系崩潰的物質 , 成為超級黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引力爆炸 , 引力崩塌的能量 。 有些物質 , 背後是一顆巨大的能量 , 引力崩塌 , 其中一些物質 , 背後的能量是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理 , 不像像物理一樣的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們沒有辦法存活下來 。 語言破壞了 , 當試著描述它所在的狀態時 , 會像什麼樣子一樣 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這可能有點像是經歷超級新星爆炸 , 但在爆炸爆炸時 , 幾百萬年來 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 在宇宙的邊緣 , 幾十億年後 , 另一邊 , 宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學論壇可以準確地描述、模型、預測 , 並且預測 , 並且預測 , 並且解釋 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學論壇可以準確地描述和預測 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個體體系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一個精確的模型 , 與其它的一模一樣 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一個超級的圖像 , 它也包含著同樣的數學關係和相同的數學關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識的知識 。 如果你不夠驚人 , 信仰就會隨著時間增長 , 那就是知識的發展 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理學的物理學有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	相同的數學和蛋白質組合 , 相同的數學和蛋白質結構 , 可以隨時間分解出來 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是不同的化學物質 , 這種化學量的化量是不同的 。 這化學的化量是不同的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構和整體的實體世界相反 , 不管是哪個地方 , 都沒有其他地方存在 , 物理世界的結構和結果 , 實際上 , 物理世界的結構和因果關係 , 實際上 , 其它的物理世界 , 不管是哪個地方 , 都沒有其他地方存在 。 這個地方 , 不論是物理世界的任何地方 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 我們如何和我們的環境相互作用 , 形成我們與其它宇宙中的其他宇宙的相互作用 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金所說的這句話 , 是真的 , 但這是錯的 , 史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 是真的 , 但它是錯的 。 重點是 , 它的確存在 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的空間 , 沒有任何特殊的物理 , 沒有任何特殊的空間 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是重要的 , 因為成長知識是資訊流程的計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 , 沒有任何東西的計算 , 計算需要一個電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要讓媒體在影響我們所記錄的知識中找到 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不容易理解 , 但 , 只是為了建立知識的解釋 , 簡單的解釋 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛剛開始測試 , 說 , 牛頓的重力約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據顯示我們過去數十億年來一直在下降 , 每一塊平方米都在地球上 , 數十億年以後 , 仍然會繼續下降 , 以至於 , 未來的數十億年 , 仍然會繼續下降 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	如我們所知 , 證據證明了所有科學領域中最基本的真相 , 就是在地球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點是充滿證據的 , 同時也含有能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星際空間中 , 三種最低的可能供應供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如同我說的 , 它是空氣的 , 它是冷的 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 , 它很冷 ; 它很冷 。
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一種錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為 , 想像一個立方體的空間 , 和我們的房子一樣大 , 太陽系就好像我們的家 , 太陽系 , 這個方塊很高 , 但那仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的重量 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠 , 說 , 一個自動駕駛的太空站 , 在那裡 , 有一群科學家被投入 , 以創造出一種開放式的知識 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 遠遠超越了科技 , 甚至將氫氣從外星分解到其他元素 , 再加入其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果物體沒有被物理定律所限制 , 那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換言之 , 它是知識的知識 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到 , 我們自動有能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再來 , 再一次 , 這對人類的觀點很明顯 , 但你要做的是用望遠鏡 , 甚至是日常設計 , 向外望遠 , 看到相同的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	若有更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見星星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些銀河系中 , 你可以做天體物理學物理學法 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學會粒子物理學 , 化學 , 等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最難的科學是生物學領域的旅行 , 因為它需要花上數億年才能達到最近的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有做過像生物學領域的旅行 , 我想我們可以每幾億年才完成 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間可以成為相同的擁抱 , 如我們所知 , 在宇宙中任何一個方塊 , 都可以成為相同的基礎 , 如同我們所知的 , 即便在宇宙中 , 都可以成為相同的狀態 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是一個獨特的可居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果交叉空間可以創造出一個開放式的流行 , 那麼幾乎所有其他環境都如此 。 所以 , 地球是地球 。 所以 , 地球是如此 , 幾乎是地球 。 所以 , 地球是如此 , 幾乎是地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	這裡有限的限制因素 , 不是資源 , 因為它們是很大的 , 而且是有限的 , 因為它們是很棒的 , 還沒有資源 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	關於宇宙的知識 , 我認為這應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有特定的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著沒有特殊的知識 , 可以讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 沒有任何特殊的知識 ,
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一顆超級新星 , 走出幾光年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們脆弱的書 , 關於脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗錯 , 最重要的是恐怖主義用武器大規模毀滅 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	而他認為文明只有50%的機會可以存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議上談到這場演說 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為 , 機率是正確的分類 , 來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他說的 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們能生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它依然不是有機會 , 而是在我們建立相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險是不是史無前例的 , 絕大多數的物種滅絕了 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 , 所有的文明已經存在了歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	若我們只想把這個特殊的定義給我們 , 我們的能力可以創造出新的解釋 , 新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 才能創造出新的解釋 , 新知識 , 來成為一個存在的空間 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我來談談我的意思 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 根據理論 , 我是物理學家 , 我只是一個層級學家 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們最好的選項就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 就像金融危機一樣 , 在經濟活動中 , 最好的選項就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 就像金融危機一樣 , 它的限制在經濟活動上花了數百億美金 , 或任何理由 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	投票者的行動 , 甚至還沒辦法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它發生了 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它發生了 , 因為在任何人意識到危險之前 , 它已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能已經太晚了 , 在1970年代末期 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放會減低到1970年代 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放會減低到1970年代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這對我來說很明顯 , 我不知道為什麼它不是公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	這是我們無法承認的 。 當我們知道一個臨時的災難時 , 會如何解決它的成本 , 比起災難的代價還要低 , 卻不會有爭議 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 , 我們還沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防措施 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個穩定的問題 , 不是只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一旦我們知道預防的預防措施 , 預防是有限的 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你一直在鼻子上發射 , 那麼科學醫學並不會教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋求治癒和專注在預防中 , 那麼它就會達到很少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界正在忙碌 , 要把氣體排放量排放到所有成本上 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	該計劃要在氣候上降低溫度 , 並鼓勵水平的氣候變遷 , 但有效率又便宜 。 有些規則 , 例如 , 在空間中 , 把陽光放射 , 讓陽光消失 , 並且鼓勵水平的生物 , 來減少溫度 , 並且在高溫度下降低溫度 , 而不是所有的成本 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些東西是可怕的研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是中央人力來面對這個問題 , 或問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們遇到的問題 , 不僅僅是解決問題 , 而是生存 , 而是生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩隻石頭 , 把石頭放在它們上 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一件事是: 「 問題是難以置信 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一方面 , 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	難以解決貧窮困境的規則經濟學家保羅姆•羅姆提出了一個大膽的想法: 「 大城市城市 , 貧窮困境 」 的規則 , 讓經濟學家保羅爾•羅姆提出一個大膽的想法: 「 大城市城市 , 貧窮困境 」 的規則 , 會如何解決貧窮問題 ?
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題 , 政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅爾羅馬的主意是:查爾斯的激進想法 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做自己的家事 , 因為他們沒有任何電力在家裡 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒有遇過這些學生 , 但是我遇到了像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	我們舉個例子 , 綠色衣服的一個例子 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我將tnelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這裡是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , 尼爾遜有機會可以在家裡發電電燈 , 但卻沒有接觸到一百歲的科技 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	在一個字中 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	糟糕的規則可以避免這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 讓人們可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則呢 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個非常低的價格下 , 價格下降低 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 , 價格低於價格 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 不管是資源 , 不管資源 , 或獎勵 , 都能讓許多其他使用者使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有些規則 , 商業賺錢的利潤很高 , 所以他們有機會可以用不同的規則 , 規則 , 商業賺錢的價格 , 所以他們有獎勵來標示更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這類規則就是手機公司的規則 , 手機公司的規則 , 監控了電話公司的規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他嘗試改變規則 , 用電力來維持現存的價格 , 但從商業和消費者中 , 消費者想要保存現有的抗議性 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他被困在有規則的情況下 , 讓他贏得解決方案 , 來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街道上被困在街道上 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試圖找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們有一些規則 , 可以改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們有一個普遍的抽象觀點 , 如果我們能給予更多的選擇 , 更多的選擇給人民 , 更多的選擇 , 和更多的國家 , 也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你想要選擇的選擇 , 比如給予領導者的選擇 , 比如給予總統選項 , 選擇要給領袖 , 選擇 , 要給領袖 , 選擇 , 要給領導者做選擇 , 比如給予總統選舉 , 選擇在經濟中有選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續消費化電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給某一方 , 或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法來改變規則 , 那會給我們一套規則 , 來改變規則 , 來改變規則 , 來改變規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到破壞規則的圖片 , 規則會讓人們在黑暗中看到 , 例如 , 規則能讓黑暗的人在黑暗中看著地球的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 看起來就像黑洞與其鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝 , 在北韓的規則 , 會讓人們在黑暗中看到 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 更深層的了解 , 文化、價值觀和信仰 , 都來自於法律和規則的規則 , 同時也更深層的了解 , 規則 , 包括法律和規則 , 同時也更深層的理解 , 文化、價值觀和信仰 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做出選擇 , 做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣性的道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	因此 , 我們可以改變人類的規則 , 可以改變我們對彼此的規則 , 更好、更好 , 更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地在海地上網 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 相較於鄰居的鄰居 , 和其他的鄰居有相同的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	兩個國家都和黑人相比 , 比如海地或多數州長 , 和墨西哥 , 有半數的居民是海地或多數民眾 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告 , 規則則是壞事 , 因為政府是弱的 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只規則糟透了 , 因為政府太強大、壓迫 , 像是北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造環境有良好的規則 , 我們就無法打破 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們必須找到方法來建立起來 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅地展現出潛力與規則的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這張圖表上 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先進的技術 , 像是鋼鐵、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採取過 , 至少在那段期間 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵傳播這些想法的傳播方式 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快的採取規則 , 減緩創新和砍掉中國 , 遠離世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 在其他國家 , 創新的國家 , 包括開發新的規則 , 中國人從那些進步開始發展新的規則 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持保持穩定 , 讓世界各地的焦慮進步 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它的平均收入是美國的平均收入 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到它大約有3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在1970年代末期 , 改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國成長在中國開始 , 中國開始非常快地接觸到美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 轉換到這個過程 , 導致在中國最劇變的變遷 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 你可以看到在上面的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是個小小的中國 , 在20世紀以來 , 中國的規則 , 大部分是中國的規則 , 由英國而來的統治 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方有數百萬人可以從主角開始工作 , 像是縫衣衫、玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入 , 增加收入的增加 , 越來越快的速度增長了 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典型的模式 , 當他們決定搬到市場模型時 , 他們決定要搬到市場模型 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 直覺地明白了對他人的重要性 , 帶來選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與市場規則相反 , 沒有任何人在中國轉移到市場規則 , 讓機會去和市場規則交易 , 讓人們可以去工作 , 去市場規則 , 讓所有人都能去做 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四種特殊的經濟區塊 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來到那裡 , 而且城市成長得很快 , 在那裡 , 城市長大得很快 , 在那裡 , 中國人也能來到那裡 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港的一個城市 , 叫做nzhen 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市裡 , 有一個塔iphone , 裡面有許多人 , 他們用勞動力 , 製造了iphone , 裡面有許多人 , 他們用勞動力 , 用勞動力來做中國人 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特殊區塊中 , 有14個沿岸公路 , 最終展示了這些地方的成功 , 人們可以選擇 , 他們被鎖定了 , 因為他們所擁有的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示成功的成功 , 讓整個經濟體系的成功 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了我們幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保留選擇給人們 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:操作正確的規模 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你就能做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你就可以做到 , 但村子的村子太小了 , 你就可以做到 , 但村子裡有數百萬人都在良好的規則上工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會 , 來看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會來回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會回顧 , 看看事情如何轉變 , 讓其他人有機會去
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新的規則 , 人們可以選擇的機會 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而且它們夠大 , 能讓所有受益者都能在好規則中 , 數百萬人一起合作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	因此提議是 , 我們稱之為 「 特定城市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一份特定的規則開始 , 規則要求吸引我們需要的人來吸引我們所需的城市 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 建造出基礎建設的電力系統 , 道路、運動、機場、房子 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會僱用那些搬到第一邊的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家庭 , 居住在那裡 , 居住永久性 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子帶來教育 , 並且得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	在那裡 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再一次地做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 , 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些是被捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要選擇給人們 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這實在是被建設在不適合居住地的城市中 , 可以建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未被居住的地點開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新冠軍中 , 但沒有人被迫活下去 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是選擇領導者 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成目標 , 我們想要領導人的選擇 , 我們想要領導者 , 我們想要領導者 , 我們想要領導者的需求 , 來解決國家之間的關係 , 例如 , 國家之間的合作 , 和英國合作 , 建立起第一個小規模的市場模型 , 然後在中國和英國之間合作 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不明確地說 , 要減少世界貧窮 , 除非我們在上世紀所受過的所有援助項目都能減少世界貧窮 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種互相合作 , 才能複製這一點 , 我們就能得到全世界各地的益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 該國有責任的責任 , 從一個國家轉移到另一個國家 , 來控制另一個國家 , 以某種程度的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是把殖民主義帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 , 但重要的是要了解到這些事物的情緒 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 可以讓我們回頭 , 能把我們的能力帶回來 , 讓我們能回頭去思考這些東西 , 可以讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭 , 能讓我們回頭
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不是殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義對殖民主義有很大的差別 , 我們對殖民主義有興趣的原因 , 就是它涉及了協議和執行 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 包括領導者 , 和那些能住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇 , 反而是爭議和執行 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習中練習 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們來找一個特定領袖 , 拉克斯特 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	他一定有機會去做古巴的古巴 , 但他沒有一個香港 , 在那裡 , 他有機會去為中國做古巴 , 但他沒有一個香港在土地上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	然而 , 在南方有一個非常特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一個區塊 , 在那裡 , 盧安達灣 , 在那裡 , 美國政府負責 , 為一塊土地設立了一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯特在加拿大的總理說: 「 看 , 黃金是可怕的主題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不加拿大 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特別的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新的城市被建造出來 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人來到這裡 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	咱們來看看香港附近 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的市民們也會搬進這個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人還會繼續回來 , 但這將會將現代經濟和現代經濟和現代經濟和現代化的經濟與現代化的連結現代化 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這種模型在哪裡被試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 , 我和非洲人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人都可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	規則是改變規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新的規則 , 讓人們不用氣候 , 和反對力 , 才能產生新的規則 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也能更清楚的承諾 , 如果他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 只要他們能做出更好的承諾 , 才能讓更多的客戶承諾 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 只要他們能做得更好的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許甚至在某種程度上 , 有點像抽菸帳號 , 你把土地放在帳戶中 , 和夥伴國家要負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲的土地 , 新城市可以被建造出來 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是一張我在海岸拍攝的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地 , 土地上有數億人可以活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個想法視為不是只有一或兩張圖片 , 而是數十億個城市 , 會在數十億人口遷移到城市中 , 成為數十億人 , 會在哪裡走向城市 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在地球上 , 如果我們看著燈光在夜晚的燈光上 , 它看起來就像世界上大部分都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我向各位說明為什麼這是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有土地的代表 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	將它轉變成一個平方形 , 代表地球上所有可靠的土地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點點代表土地 , 已經被城市佔有三十億人口居住了 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點點搬到底部 , 你可以看到 , 城市的居住區只有3%的地球上只有3%的可居住地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要建造城市 , 數十億人 , 它們會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從三分之三的土地上 , 到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅地降低人類足跡在地球上建造更多城市 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是由好規則所控制 , 人們有機會去找工作機會 , 取得一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以取得基本的電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要怎麼做才能建立起第一座城市 , 規模擴大規模 , 這樣我們才能建造出更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助一個人性 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做些細節來描述這些細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們逃離城市 , 去設計它們 。
