but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你能讓我們思考這個問題 , 假設它不是加拿大的加拿大 , 和拉克斯特 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是一名參與者 , 可能是西班牙人 , 或許古巴西是一名參與者 , 或許古巴西成為一個參與者 , 可能是四個共通點的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何作出這樣的治療 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有那麼多的預言 , 但可以輕易地做出來 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何定義這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是城市 , 製造巨大的穀物 , 讓它們能在當地的土地上做出巨大的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用這塊土地去買東西 , 像是警察、法庭、學校系統 , 以及健康照護系統 , 這使得更具吸引力的地方 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 , 讓土地更有吸引力 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 鼓勵人們幫助建構這個區塊並建立起基礎規則 , 以正確的方向為目標 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何建造出低成本和負擔得起的人 , 讓這些建築能有效率 , 確保它們安全 , 不在地震或颶風下降落地震或颶風 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節都能做到 , 但那些已經開始追蹤這些事情的人 , 已經開始追蹤這些事情 , 可能已經證明了 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 沒有任何阻礙 , 除了失敗的想像力 , 還能讓我們從真正的全球化解答中獲取 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結論這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	儘管如此 , 地球上有很多人 , 是因為有許多人在地球上 , 因為這些想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀有的物體 , 共享的意思是 , 我們每一步都少了一點 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都能得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們想到這些想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則 , 例如 , 我們的規則是如何互動彼此的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一系列的規則 , 來解釋我們如何和彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一套規則 , 來協助我們學習如何互動彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一台稅制系統 ,
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一套系統 , 在那裡 , 我們有一套系統 , 在政府辦公室裡 , 可以把土地放到政府辦公室裡 , 讓人們可以被排放在政府辦公室 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 所以 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友 , 不用多久才能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 。 謝謝 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學家先生多樣化 , 把他的團隊所發現的生物多樣性 , 帶走到一萬個基因體系中 , 他的團隊發現了很遠 , 來談談數百萬個基因組成 , 他的團隊已經發現了它 , 來探究它的地圖 , 來談談數百萬個基因組成 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物學 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 , 生物科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna和海裡的風險 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	一開始 , 我被問到幾個人關於辯論的辯論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解 , 樂觀主義者很悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我十八分鐘內 , 我們要從讀基因編碼到第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 , 來寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前 , 我們發表了一篇文章發表的第一個序列 , 叫做 「 血流感染病菌 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	從13年到4個月 , 才完成了基因組計劃 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以做同樣的基因組計畫 , 花兩到八個小時 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組已經加入了 , 包括人類的基因組 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	過去10年前的基因組定序 , 大約是10年前 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組組成 , 其中有三到五個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛剛從gordon和bettymoore基金會找到了這一年 , 成為一個來自環境器官體系的專案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 究竟到底是什麼 , 我們幾乎沒辦法把地球表面的表面放進去 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人並不了解它 , 因為它們是無形的 , 但微生物的數量大約是一半的地球生物物質 , 而所有的動物只佔了一半的地球生物物質 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不做的事 , 但如果你把海水帶到海底 , 就會發現 , 每一百萬個細菌 , 每一千萬隻病毒就有一百萬個細菌 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	超過5000種微生物物種被分為兩年前 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	然後我們開始了第二次的探險 , 嘗試樣本海洋的攝影機 , 拍攝200英哩外的海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海海岸、加勒比海海岸、加勒比海海岸、加勒比海海岸、加勒比海海岸、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海、加勒比海等等 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱苦的 , 我們在一艘船上做這件旅行 , 讓年輕人了解科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們把海水拿到實驗室裡 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 在岩維爾 , 我們收集不同的濾水器 , 然後把它們的dna帶到我們的實驗室 , 每24小時就可以排列出一億個字母 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這麼做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 認為我們眼睛中的視覺色素 , 只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中有著不同的生物 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有物種都在海洋的溫暖區域中 , 用陽光來源 , 用太陽光來照顧它們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 到一桶海水 , 我們發現了130萬種新的基因 , 和許多五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這張照片放到空氣中 , 由土地基金會給了 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機或關閉節目中 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們收集了數十億微生物 , 僅僅是紐約市的一棟大樓 , 收集了數十億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於這個階段的過程中 , 一直以來序列 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料集中 , 我們在海洋中看到了多樣性的樣本 , 大約在200英哩內 , 看到了巨大的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	在不同溫度上 , 不同的溫度會降低 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度溫度降低溫度 , 溫度是紅色的溫度 , 我們發現有很大的差別在溫度和冷水樣本中 , 有很大的差別 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件令人驚訝的是 , 我們有微小的光線 , 可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測基礎 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些從區域到地區的重大區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不令人驚訝 , 在深海中 , 最藍色的光線 , 會看到藍色的光線 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當大量的綠光時 , 它們會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們更有可能在極端中移動到紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了嘗試 , 了解我們基因的基因資料 , 我們將所有的資料包含全部的資料 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 將所有資料包含在地球上 , 超過一半的基因資料 , 將所有的資料包含在地球上 , 超過一半的基因資料包含了全部的基因資料 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因放到基因家庭裡 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們發現了新的家庭 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每種新的樣本 , 我們將這些新品種的基因組合 , 帶給這些新的家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們在這個星球上最早的階段 , 發現了基本的基因、組成和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約有2900萬個基因 , 我們只有2億個基因 , 只有大約29萬個基因 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物組合在一起 , 我們可能大概有一千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因不僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在基因組合的觀點中 , 基因組合的觀點是不同的構造 , 這些基因組合的構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna組成dna序列的能力在過去十年或兩年間 , 已經改變了 , 相同的dna序列在過去的十年或兩年間 , 已經改變了 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們的第一個思想合成基因組 , 在1995年時 , 基因組合成基因組合成基因組 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 說: 「 我心我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	hemophilus有一千八百個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 或500個 , 另一個500 , 另一個500 , 一個比較小的基因 , 會產生最小的組合嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉變性的突破 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯只是小小的dna , 在基因編碼中被遺傳密碼 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果在基因中間的中間 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 把所有基因的基因放進去 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能定義一個基本或不必要的基因 , 只能定義一個基本或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智能方法 , 來和數十三個相關的基因組連結在一起 , 我們試圖將這些相互聯繫起來 , 來看看他們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	然後我們發現了173個基因 , 只有173種基因 , 只有173種基因 , 只有173種基因 , 只有173個基因 , 只有173個基因 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	一旦我們忽略了細胞寄生蟲 , 它就擴展了 , 即便當我們研究核心基因的大約310個位置時 , 就會擴展 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此 , 我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 可能300到400個基因組 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法是要建立一個人造的染色體 , 我們必須用這種方式來建立一個人工染色體 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現合成準確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆.史密斯、我的同事們 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成5 , 000個鹼基對病毒 , 只有兩週期內 , 只有兩週期內 , 只有一個兩週期 , 只有一個兩週期 , 只有一個兩週期 , 只有一個兩週期 , 就是它的序列和生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 我們把病毒粒子的基因組成dna開啟 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒的病毒在一年前發生了 , 但只有一個十分之一 , 才有十分之一 , 才能做到 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這種軟體現在已經建立了自己的硬體 , 我們有生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始評估這個區域 , 我最近在參議院委員會和委員會上 , 特別委員會委員會議員 , 委員會委員會議員 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實生活在心中 , 和人們的想像力是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何病毒都是由基因組組成的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就會想到伊波拉病毒或小小pox , 但dna從這個機體的dna沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使某人製造了小型生物基因組 , 那dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的安全部門是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯盟 , 致力於嘗試創造生物戰事 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這研究真的被關注 , 不該有小活動 , 才能讓設計師病毒在未來發生 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就有可能 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是可能性細胞 , 在十年內 , 我們已經有的可能性 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在已經製造了數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以把這些人造染色體和基因放進這個人工染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你如何把所有人都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有了一組合理的組合系統 , 將這些碎片換成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是來自有機體的durans , 可以將三百萬輻射輻射射射輻射 , 無法殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	將它的基因組排放到24小時後 , 染色體的染色體已經被爆炸了 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上生存 , 可能在外太空中 , 存在於我們的旅行中 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一張玻璃碎片 , 超過一半以上百萬輻射的輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 雖然微生物在底部的微生物會變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一個實際的圖片:這張圖顯示了基因組 , 一百七十萬種輻射輻射 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體其實是被摧毀的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同一個dna自動組裝在24小時後 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千萬種不同的物種 , 可能有數以千計的物種 , 可能有數以千計的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到細胞中 , 不是基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅為了了解生物學的基礎 , 而是為了希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 我們所序列的第三個生物 , 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量源源是氫氣 , 它的能量來源是氫氣 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 可以從二氧化碳回來 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 用碳從大氣中抽取石油 , 用碳從大氣層轉換成生物聚合物 , 或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體存在於碳氫和氧氣中 , 而我們用的是減少能量來製造氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	另外 , 有許多條路可以用來製造甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	而杜邦有一項主要的計劃 , 用來捕捉並將甲烷從氣體中轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的時間內 , 我認為 , 我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造出一百萬個不同的染色體 , 像是 「 組合性基因組合 」 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合性基因組 」 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合性基因組合 」 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合性基因組 」 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合性基因學 」 。 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 「 組合性基因組 」 , 因為這些新領域 , 叫做 " 組合性基因組 " 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你選擇通過篩選 , 不論你是否被篩檢 , 或化學產品 , 或是化學產品 , 或僅僅是殘疾 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的角色 , 才能了解這些基因的角色 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用 , 來製造氫氣直接從陽光 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用光合作用氧氣 , 我們有氧氣濃度的氫氣 , 我們認為它會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞 , 製造乙醇 , 酵素分解成簡單糖和酵素 , 分解成簡單糖 , 和酵素 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖 , 和酵素分解 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在大型實驗室使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	在環境中 , 化學成分比我們最好的化學家所製造出的化學還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的源源 , 可能是食物的源源 , 希望是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 , 希望能是食物的源源 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用道德和政策研究 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們從1999年開始開始實驗 , 直到我們完成了一篇關於人類的實驗 , 直到我們完成了一整年的實驗 , 直到我們完成一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個重大宗教都參與這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為這些宗教領袖用他們的文字描繪成法律書 , 卻沒有辦法找到任何東西來做這些實驗 , 為了我們要做的事 , 他們也無法找到任何東西來做這些實驗 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前 , sloan基金會已經資助一個多項科學團隊的規則 , 如我自己應該在這個區域工作的 , 我們試著為我們建立好的例子 , 來證明風險和益處 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了恐怖生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能設計出能生產乾淨能源 , 也許革新國家能做什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說 , 快樂和成功是根源於我們前面的一個:我們向前走的路徑 , 向過去、現在和未來的方向 , 他建議我們將這一步驟改善我們的人生 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦 , 企業 , 快樂 , 心靈 , 心理學 , 科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo預設了一個健康的照護 。

life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是充滿誘惑的 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 再來 , 反思 , 爭論 , 反映 , 反映 , 反映 , 反映 , 反映 , 現在 , 反映出去 , 反映出去 , 反映出去 , 反映出去 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的熱情讓美德陷入熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女孩在一年內被性侵略性侵略性侵略性侵略 , 直到婚姻 , 感謝喬治布希大部分 , 60% , 一直到婚姻 謝謝喬治 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大多數人都沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	所以 , 承諾要承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們嘗試四歲孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	牠們可以有兩種棉花糖 , 但如果他們等到實驗員回來後 , 他們就能有兩種 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子都在誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們退化之後 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	史丹佛的同事在史丹福大學的同事 , 花了14年的時間 , 試著找出與這些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	孩子們有很大的差異 , 在許多方面 , 都有大量的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒了250位的孩子 , 保留了250點 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這實在太大了 。 這就像是一整套不同的智商標準 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到麻煩 。 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且決心的關鍵 。 我今天的關鍵是 , 為你帶來的關鍵是 , 他們是未來的 , 而不是現在的鑰匙 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間是怎樣的呢 ? 這就是我今天要談的內容 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	觀點是人類體驗的研究 , 或時間分裂 , 或時間分裂 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動和無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化之間、國家之間、社會階級之間、社會階級之間之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 牠們會變得偏見 , 因為你學會會被偏見 , 因為你學會會被偏見 。
what determines any decision you make ?	決定你要做什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 讓你做出一個決定 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只會發生在什麼事 , 以及你所感受到的是什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們在這個形式上做決定時 , 我們會稱之為 「 自願者 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現況是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在過去 , 「 我所經歷過的情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會把這些人稱為 「 過去原始人 」 , 因為他們專注在哪裡 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對於其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來原理 」 , 他們的焦點放在哪裡 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 矛盾的觀點是有影響力的決定 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有這種偏見的觀點 , 已經有了這些偏見 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 , 其中有兩種方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式是過去的 , 兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面上 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以被掌控 , 專注於人生的喜悅 , 不論是你生命的喜悅 , 或虛擬主義者 , 不論你的人生是如何被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可能是未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或你是超越未來的 , 生命早在死亡後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 可以改變時間觀點 , 就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快的 , 什麼是最佳的時代 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度對未來有高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而在現代主義中 , 現代主義是如此 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最樂觀的形式就是你從過去所得到的正面向你傳遞給你的根源 , 你把你的家人、身分和你的個人連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來的目的就是要追求新的挑戰 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現場表達出來的能量是能量 , 去探索自己、人、人、感知 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點 , 都比正面更有負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來的犧牲成功是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 。 他們犧牲了家庭時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲個人的優勢 。 他們犧牲了個人的婚姻 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活著工作、成就 , 以及控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我肯定會和一些tedsterstersters談話 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我來說是很糟糕的 。 我成長在南布朗克斯區的一個貧窮的孩子 , 一個貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯區的貧窮小孩子 , 和現在一樣 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我身為一個未來的主導人 , 向前邁進 , 做這些犧牲 , 因為教師介入了 , 讓未來的方向變得更好 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那棉花糖 , 因為如果你等待你會得到兩位 , 直到我學到平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我已經加上了專注 , 一直以來 , 比我更有創意 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更高興 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更高興 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想要說 , 我們正在應用這個世界問題:改變了許多世界問題:改變了家庭衝突的數量 , 例如 , 改善貧窮的狀況 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 , 改善性別 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 「 增加五百分之一 」 , 改善貧窮的環境 , 改善家庭衝突 , 例如 「 變遷 」 的原因 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:很多人生的謎題都可以解決 , 透過了解你的時間觀點和其他人 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果是很簡單的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少人的頭條新聞 ?  「 長期新聞 」 計畫收集了這些故事 , 不只重要 , 而是在2010年 , 在ted2010年 , 他高速追求了數十年來的新聞 , 來影響我們未來的未來 。

they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	他們從幾公里長大到大小的公里 , 以至於大大的距離 。

and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一種身體 , 它有著很長的感染力 , 看過地球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大的厚度 , 大氣層 , 實際上 , 它的表面環境被相信更像我們在地球上的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 在地球上 , 或至少在地球上 , 沒有任何其他的身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層是大氣層 , 例如甲烷 , 大氣層 , 大氣層是大氣層 , 大氣層是大氣層 , 像甲烷和乙烷一樣 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在大氣層中釋放大氣中 , 他們的產品會加入結合 , 來製造混合物 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種仇恨是完全全球化的 , 它完全是全球化的 , 完全是全球化的 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能在表面上看到我們眼睛的視覺區塊 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些微小的粒子 , 在我們到達克斯坦尼之前 , 經過數十億年 , 一直到地表面積 , 加速到表面上 , 加入表面 , 加入表面上 , 加入表面 , 加上數十億年的溫度 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 如同等 , 土壤 , 或石油 , 或石油 , 我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們所懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 。 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。 這些分子特別是甲烷和乙烷 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是泰坦水在地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 這種情況是可以避免任何陽光從上升到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是350度 , 表面的溫度是攝氏350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管如此寒冷 , 你可能會雨下降落在土地上 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 它能製造峽谷 , 它可以形成河流和水晶 , 它可以創造峽谷 , 它可以形成河流和水晶 , 它能創造峽谷 , 它能形成河流和水晶 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以穿高山頂高山峰和山頂的高山山峰和山峰 , 等到下降到低地 , 然後停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 , 在土衛六是黑暗的 , 高於地球上 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很冷 , 很冷 , 很冷 , 很冷 , 可能是雨林 , 可能是雨水 , 你可能在拉克密西根州的海岸上 , 和雨水混合 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在titan的表面上看到的 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在titan的表面上所發現的 , 雖然它不是細節的表面 , 但它和細節相比 , 非常有趣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 像克斯坦尼一樣 , 一直以來 , 像克斯坦尼一樣 , 一直以來 , 一直以來都是如此 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如同我說的 , 它有厚厚、強大的氣體 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張圖片是土衛六的背景 , 靠著太陽 , 和美麗的背景相反 。

this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 實際上 , 其實是一顆老鼠 , 但在土衛六的表面上有非常小的表面 。

they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像是被拆開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到任何線條 , 就會表示 , 有一個折磨 , 比如錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以 , 它一直在改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到六個月後 , 我們進入軌道上 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人都被視為 「 泰坦 」 的高點 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	當時的確是衛星探測器 , 它在土地上飛行了7年 , 太陽系中 , 我們將它送到大氣層 , 用在土地上 , 花了兩半半小時 , 才能將它降到大氣層 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下 , 這到底是多麼重要的 。

it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很明顯的是 , 在我的腦海裡 , 這場景象是 , 在美國和歐洲 , 最悲慘的是 , 不幸的是 , 這個事件應該被慶祝在美國和歐洲 , 悲傷的是 , 這還不夠 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這對另一個原因很有意義 。 這是個國際的任務 , 尤其是國際運動 , 尤其是國際任務 , 尤其是英國的演奏 , 還有德國人 , 特別是美國的表演者 , 尤其是英國口音 , 還有德國人 , 尤其是美國的表演 , 還有德國人的表演 , 尤其是在英國口音中 , 和德國的演講 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這句話是 「 聯合國 」 的意思:一個真正的聯合國集合起來 , 成為一個真正的聯合國 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 一個行星的行星系統 , 對人類而言 , 真的很難去探索一個行星 , 並且要來了解一個行星系統 , 對於人類的歷史 , 已經不可思議了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我在談論它時 , 要談談它 。

but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	不論如何 , 探測器在下面進行測量 , 它也拍攝了大氣層的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你們 , 看到的第一張圖片是怎麼樣的 , 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這很震驚 , 因為我們希望其他的照片從軌道上移動 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一個模糊的模式 , 地理模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一個可以形式的液體 , 可以用液體來形容的 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 然後你可以看到它們的頻道 。

and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?

and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它在一個平面的黑暗區域中被扭曲 , 而它不會被吸引 , 所以它不是液體的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	原來的底層是泥巴 , 基本上就是泥巴 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一種不穩定的地面 , 它被液態甲烷所影響 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這樣的情況 , 這種材料已經被廢棄了大量的土地 , 在這些頻道上 , 我們看到的 , 已經累積了數十億年來填補在低地底下 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是 「 獵物原本 」 的原始 。

where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡呢 ? 更令人難以置信 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好吧 , 這是我們一百公里的紀錄片 , 顯示這些沙丘 , 它們是一百公尺高的地點 , 分離距離數公里 , 遠距離 , 距離幾公里 。

so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 難以置信 , 直到最後 , 我們看到湖泊在極端地區 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	南極地區有個湖景 。

so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎是液體 , 有些原因我們不了解 , 或至少這季節時 , 很顯然地在南極洲 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	總之 , 我們會發現泰坦是個很奇妙的星球 , 但奇怪的 , 地球本身 , 和豐富的地球 。 它是外星生物 , 和豐富的地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到泰坦的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它是泰坦的大小 , 你可以看到它在英格蘭的大小 , 你可以看到它是泰坦的大小 , 你可以看到它是泰坦的大小 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常明白的 , 很明顯的 , 它的表面很明顯地被破碎 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常地質的活躍體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在南極 , 我們發現了這座雕像的南極 , 我們發現了這座雕像南極的地方 , 我們在南極找到了這個系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋 , 這些碎片被包含有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個地區 , 南極地區 , 高溫度是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 地球的熱帶比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拿到更多的圖片時 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 冰粒會擴散到太空中 , 數百英里外的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把顏色的影像放進來 , 我們會看到這些噴射流感 , 實際上 , 我們看到 , 這些噴射流量很高 , 我們看到這些噴射流量相當多 , 在土地上千英里外 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我研究了一些類似這樣的圖像 , 像這樣 , 像這樣 , 想出了其他的結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到了結論 , 這些噴泉可能是從土地底下噴出的液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有有機物質、有機物質 , 和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有機會可以適應活有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系裡的發現 , 無論是在土衛二 , 或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學的意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能示範一下 , 這種基因會發生什麼事 , 不只一次 , 而是兩倍 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 這意味著 , 隨著時間 , 會發生在宇宙中 , 和其它137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一的星球 , 是我們知道的 , 地球是唯一的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 目前我們所知的唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們在1968年被阿波羅8號太空人所拍攝 , 會記得這張很有名的照片 , 被阿波羅8號太空人所拍攝 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次 , 地球是從太空中拍攝的 , 它對我們對地球來說是很大的衝擊 , 在宇宙中 , 有著巨大的衝擊 , 在宇宙中 , 我們對地球的責任感也對我們有著巨大的影響 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡斯丁尼做了一個相同的照片 , 沒有人眼前看到的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的表面 , 從土星的角度來看 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張圖片中 , 你看不出藍色的圖像 , 你看到了太陽的背景 , 你看到了太陽的重覆 , 實際上 , 由於土衛二的消息 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這張美麗的影像還不夠聰明 , 我們就能夠在地球上 , 以土星的圖像來描繪出它的美麗影像 , 和我們自己的星球的影像 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的看法 , 看著我們自己從阿富汗 , 並且捕捉到我們的小小 , 藍色星球的周圍世界 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從這段旅程發現的觀點 , 可能是最後的結果 , 我們從這段旅程發現的一半世紀前 , 終於找到了這個旅程 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 只有15%的人在這個短片內 , 世界各地出現了大量的地圖圖片 , 世界各地的地圖和未知道路 。 這段短篇演講中 , 谷歌的愛滋病患者 , 在這個短片內 , 發現了全球的地圖和未知道路 。 在這個短期的演講中 , 谷歌的globe的使用地圖繪製了世界各地的地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉里斯坦•卡爾加達:製作地圖對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 塞爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼納爾尼
