but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 ,
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地圖在地圖上是很困難的 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國在世界各地的地圖上都有許多問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志願者用一個新的軟體來繪製一萬三千公里的路、三千個醫院、邏輯和信念 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	新軟體他們用了嗎 ? google地圖 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖是一套科技 , 讓每個人都能在地圖上我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有的道路 , 從路線到河流 , 從學校到商店 , 到街角店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主 , 諾貝爾獎得主 , 大部分發展中國家 , 都要把大量未知的鑰匙轉移到經濟利益 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美元的土地產量不管在印度
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	去年 , 僅僅有數以千計的使用者在170個國家收集了數以千計的資料 , 創造出一個地圖 , 不可思議的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這種方式可以透過熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些地圖 , 是由使用者所建立的 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們說的 , 人們正在繪製世界在170個國家中 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑在塞內加爾的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	再回到家 , 加羅拉 , 在班加羅拉 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這就是計算幾何學的結果 , 包括計算幾何學 , 辨識和機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 一個使用者 , 有一百個使用者 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這個邀請給我們地球上百分之七十的受歡迎 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴西亞的巴西人問了為什麼我們只關注暴力抗議去阻止阻止阻止阻止阻止阻止阻止障礙的商業活動 。 巴西人會說: 「 巴西 , 巴西人有一天會帶和平來阻止障礙 。 」
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、樂趣、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞:注意非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	在過去的八年中 , 我已經把我的人生記錄到以色列和巴勒斯坦人試圖結束衝突的用和平的意義 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:那是巴勒斯坦甘地嗎 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦非暴力抗爭呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 通常我剛從中東開始 , 我花了幾年的時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防禦他們的土地和水資源 , 用非暴力來防護他們的土地和水資源 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖要讓大量的國家非暴力運動最終佔領、建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種區塊在地面和平和平抗爭運動中發生了什麼事 , 卻成功了 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我要來談談注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 你注意力的力量 , 你的注意力 , 你的注意力 , 你的注意力 , 以及在西非暴力運動的力量 , 在西岸 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大規模的非暴力行為 , 要開始採取非暴力行為 , 但對我們來說 , 要開始採取非暴力行為 , 而是為了我們開始關注這些人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明這點 , 帶給你們這個村莊叫布魯斯的村子 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣布 , 要建造一個隔離障礙 , 這條障礙會在村落前面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	牠們會失去40%的土地 , 同時也失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地 , 所以他們失去了40%的土地 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過鼓舞當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗議活動 , 來阻止發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片段 , 讓你可以感覺一下 , 在地面上有某種意義 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知牆壁會把巴勒斯坦婦女分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布魯斯 , 我們發現牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人來說 , 事實上 , 創造出一個解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請到一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹所加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:沒有什麼比非暴力反對 , 更不暴力反抗 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推出軍人 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須擁抱我們的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈瑪斯派對:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要將它傳播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	主題:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和普通的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞報導: 「 沿著條件繼續下去 。 」
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播觀眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活的 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像布拉威 , 每次都在拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的行動主義者:我確保我們將會死亡 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身上 , 有些人甚至連同事都沒有 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止它 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	主題:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴基:當我第一次聽到關於布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝 , 在2003年 , 國際媒體已經失敗了 , 以至於一篇關於布德魯斯的事件 , 發生了七年前的事 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 數十個月後 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的區分 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的區塊 , 以以色列和巴勒斯坦之間的區分 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	巴勒斯坦的社區在耶路撒冷的抗議中 , 巴勒斯坦街坊 , 和巴勒斯坦的社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事中 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成很深刻的影響 , 不管在巴勒斯坦有沒有暴力的可能性 , 或甚至存活在巴勒斯坦 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗藥性和非暴力抗爭是劇場的一場演說 , 它們都是戲劇的形式 , 讓觀眾看到它們的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一的一群人 , 會對巴勒斯坦的議題感到難以置信 , 它就變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓這些民眾團體變成難以避免的 , 對非暴力的領導者而言 , 讓這些人成為他們所謂的 「 非暴力者 」 , 它會變得非常困難 , 非暴力的領導者 , 會讓這些民眾失望 , 變成非常困難的 , 非暴力的領導者 , 讓這些人成為他們所謂的 「 非暴力者 」 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的注意力可能會在房間裡沒有驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子變得更大膽 , 要讓孩子變得更大膽 , 要讓你的孩子變得更大膽 , 要讓孩子變得更大 , 讓孩子變得更大 , 讓孩子變得更大 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	童年心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經學會兒童心理學家稱之為功能行為 , 因為孩子已經學會兒童心理學家稱之為功能行為 , 因為孩子已經學會兒童心理學家稱之為功能行為 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或把注意力轉移到他們的孩子身上 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區的行為和國家都可以受到影響 , 依賴國際社群選擇聚焦注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在中東地區 , 將非暴力行為轉換成一個功能行為 , 讓非暴力行為更加關注在現今的非暴力行為 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落裡 , 我看到了一部電影的影響力 , 甚至一部紀錄片能影響到它的轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉威爾的村莊 , 社區正面臨著非常類似的波拉威 , 和布德魯斯一樣 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去了許多土地 , 沒有自由取得 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們一直在使用非暴力行為 , 兩年來 , 因為沒有人注意到 , 沒有人會注意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一套螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們會說出最好的示範 , 和隔離的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們在電影裡看到了布達德魯斯的紀錄片 , 感覺到 , 人們在乎他們所做的事 , 人們會在乎他們所做的事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	以色列之名為索利亞里 , 這意味著在伊斯蘭國和平運動 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這種運動的領導者已經用布德魯斯作為一個主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導了非暴力事件的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉jeh和seh和slidarjeh的例子 , 即便是獨立電影可以扮演一個角色 , 讓非暴力轉變成功能行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 強大媒體玩家的力量 , 只要他們開始覆蓋週期的非暴力領導者 , 會變得更明顯、更有價值觀、有效 , 和他們的工作中有所不同 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的事情是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力 , 他們是隱形的 , 就像從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 我先舉手 , 若我們這麼做 , 他們會多重 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們多大 , 他們的影響會成長在巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於阻擋了情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證明了非暴力工作在像布魯斯那樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 讓他們能證明它在任何地方都能成功 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙沙克有個很簡單又強大的模型 , 激勵領導力的領導力 , 從黃金圓圈和 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金、馬丁路德金 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	商業、企業、商業、企業、企業、企業、領導力、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙.斯坦克:偉大的領導者鼓勵行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所假設時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠達成這些假設時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年 , 一年後 , 他們比所有競爭者都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一台電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的能力 , 相同的顧問 , 同一家公司 , 同一部媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德•金恩領導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一的男人 , 他是美國最偉大的人 , 他肯定不是唯一的受害者 , 而他肯定不是唯一的受害者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼 , 萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力 , 控制權力的人 , 在某些其他的團隊中 , 更好的資金是: 「 萊兄弟可以想出控制 。 」
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成人權力的飛行員 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 甚至深深地改變了我的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果或馬丁路德•金恩或馬丁路德•金恩 , 他們都認為 , 行為和溝通的方式是一樣的 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	完全相反的對其他人而言 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把這個世界最簡單的點子轉化 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ? 如何 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領袖能夠鼓舞其他人 , 卻沒有 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我定義一下很快的詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 每一個組織 , 都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不管你是否稱它為 「 不論你是否稱之為合理化的價值觀點 」 或 「 不管你是如何 」 或 「 不管你 」 的意思 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 很少人或組織知道他們為何要這麼做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	「 為什麼 」 我不指 「 為何要做利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 結果是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的信仰是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為何有人在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們所思考的方式 , 溝通的方式就是從外面來 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最明顯的事物中從最清晰的事物到最清晰的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵領袖和鼓舞人士 , 不管他們的產業 , 都不管他們的產業 , 不管他們的產業 , 都認為 , 和激勵領袖和鼓舞的組織 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我使用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易了解 , 每個人都能得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	假如蘋果和其他人一樣 , 會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們是美麗的設計 , 簡單使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一個嗎 ? 「 啊 ! 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這是最大的銷售量 , 最大的銷售量是 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣 , 最大的銷售方式是這樣 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說 , 我們說我們是怎樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說 , 我們說我們是怎樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說 , 我們是怎麼樣的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們會說 , 我們會說什麼樣的行為、購買、投票 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 最好的律師 , 我們總是為了客戶和我們對客戶做事業 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它很棒的氣體 , 它有天氣層面 , 可以買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這就是蘋果實際上溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品很簡單 , 使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是為了製造偉大的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同了嗎 ? 你準備好要買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是逆轉資訊的秩序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它證明了我們是人們不買你做的事 , 人們買了你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋為何在這個房間裡的每個人都非常舒服購買電腦蘋果 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但是我們也非常舒適地購買一個來自蘋果電腦的蘋果電腦 , 或來自蘋果電腦的手機 , 或來自蘋果電腦的手機 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如同我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一台電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何一個競爭對手的競爭 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者對這些產品都很平等 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 高速公路出現了平面螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們可以用平面螢幕電視來做平面螢幕 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	幾年來 , 他們都在製作螢幕偵測器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾出了三個玩家和pdas , 他們製造出很好的品質產品 , 且他們能做出完美的產品 , 且沒有人買了 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一個mp3的玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會買一台電腦公司的一台電腦公司 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你有的人做事業 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你相信的人合作 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:沒有我告訴你的 , 是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這一切都在生物學的基礎上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細觀察人類大腦的交叉 , 會發現人類大腦其實被破碎成三個主要組件 , 完全與黃金圓圈結合 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 都應對 「 什麼 」 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質負責我們所有的理性、分析思維和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊會讓我們的大腦負責 , 我們的肢體大腦都負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也對人類的行為有責任 , 所有的決策 , 都沒有能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面交流時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、有利、事實和事實 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不開動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通到大腦的部分時 , 我們會直接告訴大腦控制行為的部分 , 然後我們讓人們可以藉由溝通的方式來處理我們所說的行為 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決定從哪裡來 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給人一些事實和細節 , 說: 「 我知道 , 所有事實和細節都說 , 但那並不感覺 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 「 感覺 」 對不對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦的一部分 , 控制決策不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好的辦法是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不好 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	有時候你會說你和你的心靈魂有關 , 或是你會帶著你的心靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭向你們解釋 , 那些不是其他身體的部分控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都在你的肢體大腦中 , 控制決策和非語言的大腦 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你做這事 , 你會怎麼做 , 人們會去投票給你 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣地 , 目標不僅僅是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 , 目標是要賣給那些相信你相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 你知道 , 如果你僱用那些相信你相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你相信的人 , 他們會為你的錢做工作 , 還會為你帶來血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	此外 , 除了萊特兄弟 , 這裡還有更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初期 , 電力飛行的追求力力飛行就像是今日的旅行 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley , 我們假設 , 是成功的成功 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三樣東西:受試者、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是相同的三件事 , 讓我們探究它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley已經5萬美金給了五萬美金的飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在smithsonian和smithsmithsonian工作 , 他知道所有大型的思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的智慧金錢可以找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追蹤了他 , 每個角落都在追隨他 , 每個人都在追隨他 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	我們從來沒有聽過samuelpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠 , 在華盛頓俄亥俄州 , 俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾維爾 , 他們沒有我們考慮到成功的工具 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 從他們的腳踏車購買 , 沒有錢 ; 由自行車店而來的學生 , 沒有錢 ; 和他們從自行車店工作的同事 , 沒有任何人 , 住在萊特兄弟的團隊大學教育 , 不論是誰 , 或wilbur , 都沒錢 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差異是 , 維爾和瓦爾是由一個原因所驅使 , 由一個信念所驅動 , 由一個信念來驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這個飛行機器 , 它將會改變世界 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要很有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追尋結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富有的財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	然後 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信在萊特兄弟的夢想中 , 他們有血液、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了付錢而付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說 , 每次有多少次 , 他們就必須拿五組零件 , 因為那就是他們有多少次要拿五個零件 , 因為那就是他們要拿五組零件的時候 , 因為那就是他們會拿到來供應的一部分 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在12月17日1903年12月17日 , 萊兄弟飛行了 , 沒有人願意去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明 , 萊斯萊恩出錯了:那天 , 萊特兄弟飛行了 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個很驚人的發現 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一次 , 他沒有賺錢 , 他沒有很有名 , 所以他辭了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信的東西 , 你就會吸引那些相信你相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信的人 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做 「 法律 」 的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道這個法律 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	第一 , 兩百分半的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們早期的採取者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期 , 你的大部份和你的遲早 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們買到手機的唯一原因是 , 因為你不能買到手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各處各地 , 各個不同的地方都在不同的地方 , 但 , 創新告訴我們:如果你想要大規模市場的執行 , 或大規模市場的執行 , 你就無法做到這一點 , 直到你達成這個目標 , 到達十五到18%的市場制度 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新商業的反應是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試驗超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都只有10%的人只能說 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述他們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就好像 , 「 喔 , 他們只能得到它 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你在做商業之前 , 和那些沒有人做事業的人 , 會怎麼找到 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 在這裡 , 這個小小的差距 , 你可以看到 , 早期的大部份不會嘗試 , 直到有人嘗試過第一件事 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採取者 , 他們很舒適地做出這些決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒適地做出那些直覺決策 , 是由他們所相信的世界所驅動 , 而不是產品所得到的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人是站在四個小時購買iphone的人 , 他們第一次出櫃時 , 只要走進商店 , 就可以買一台iphone , 然後買了一台iphone , 然後買了一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上 , 即便他們才剛出發 , 即使那技術是可行的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技很棒 , 他們也做得到 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買了你做什麼 , 他們買了你做什麼 ; 他們買了你為什麼要做的事 , 他們買了你所做的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們相信的東西 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	有人買了iphone在六小時之內 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們想要如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個例子 , 一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功 , 一個著名的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 有名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 第一步 , 是金錢和對人對市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從那時起到八到九年前 , 到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 沒錯 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用 「 推動詞 」 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西放在我垃圾堆的垃圾桶裡 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 股票大約30到40美金 , 然後就被丟棄了 , 以至於30到40美金 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它已經超過六個 , 只剩下幾個小小的案件 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看到 , 當tivo發出他們的產品告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 暫停生活電視節目 , 錄音節目 , 電視節目 , 記錄你的觀看習慣 , 沒有你會問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	古典的主人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不需要它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是這樣的人 , 若你是那種人 , 不管你生活中的每個方面 , 我們都有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它暫停生活的電視 , 網頁 , 記住電視 , 紀錄你的觀看習慣等等 , 等等 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你所做的事 ; 他們買了你做什麼 ; 他們買了你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的只是服務你所做的事 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 關於創新的例子 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 二十五萬人在華盛頓特區去聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們被送出沒有邀請 , 沒有網站去查查日子 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個偉大的人 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一在美國受苦的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有告訴人們需要改變美國的事 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走過來告訴別人他相信什麼 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	人們相信他相信他所相信的原因 , 他們給了他們自己 , 讓人們相信他的想法 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人可以說出更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	不久 , 兩萬五千人在右邊的時間聽見他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人給他看 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們展現出自己 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國 , 讓他們能在8個小時站在8個小時站在華盛頓的陽光上 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界中有兩種法律:那些是由一個較高權威和那些人所組成的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有法律 , 都是由強權者所組成的法律 , 我們生活在一個世界中 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	公民權利運動是完美的幫助他把他帶到生命中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤他 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他給了我一個 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽政治人物 , 用它們的12point計畫來做 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為那裡有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權力權力的權力 , 但那些領導人會鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們會追蹤那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們想要做 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	這些人是從 「 為何 」 開始的 , 有能力來啟發他們或找到其他人 , 鼓舞他們 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記得你停車在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 你要怎麼知道你在哪裡 ? 要知道你在哪裡 ? 要知道你在右邊的神經細胞 , 和記憶和想像力有關 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•布吉斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們公開車子時 , 我們如何記得我們停車在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡有個問題面向家人 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他腦中的發生 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬迴開始 , 在黃色 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在阿茲海默症 , 像阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住事情包括你停車的位置 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	在拉丁文 「 海馬 」 之後 , 它的名字是 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和其他的大腦一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 讓彼此溝通 , 讓彼此溝通 , 互相溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩個細胞組成的 , 它們非常緊密相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家已經開始了解 , 大腦的記憶力是如何運作的 , 透過記錄從個人神經元中 , 或老鼠、老鼠或老鼠 , 來了解空間記憶如何運作 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像我們在記錄這隻老鼠的海馬體的神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電力時 , 會有一個紅點點點 , 點點點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是這個神經元知道 , 當老鼠進入一個特定的地方時 , 牠的環境就會發生 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它的訊號會傳送到大腦的訊號 , 讓大腦傳送一個小電擊 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們能顯示神經元的功能是動物的軌跡 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從很多不同的神經元開始 , 我們會看到不同神經元的不同神經元 , 當動物在環境中移動時 , 會看到不同的神經元 , 就像在這個方形的盒子裡 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 把它們的圖片放到大腦裡 , 跟大腦說: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時需要電動活動在他們的大腦監控 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在小鎮上玩電玩遊戲 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當它們穿過特定的位置時 , 就會開始發送電脈衝動 , 讓它們在那座小鎮上發電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 細胞知道哪一個位置是哪裡的 , 哪個位置是哪裡的 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線是很重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 頂端的牆壁箱子裡的頂端 , 會在箱子之間的牆壁之間打開 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展這個盒子時 , 飛行器就會擴展 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	一旦接觸到南方 , 就會有牆壁接近 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一個牆放進盒子裡 , 另外一個牆壁就在盒子裡 , 另外一個牆壁在這個盒子裡 , 在那裡 , 牆壁就在盒子裡的細胞壁上 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測 , 會讓海馬體周圍的距離和方向的距離 , 對海馬體來說是很重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	實際上 , 在海馬體上 , 細胞發現了海馬體的特定位置 , 牠會在海馬迴中找到它的特定位置 , 去偵測哪些特定距離 , 或距離 , 到海馬體 , 到海馬迴 , 牠會在探測到海馬迴 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的圖片是 , 你可以看到 , 它的火焰會在周圍的牆壁上移動 , 不論是邊緣或牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 即便是邊緣 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 不論是邊緣 , 或邊緣的牆壁 , 都可以看見 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞在右邊邊緣 , 不管是左邊邊緣的牆 , 或牆壁或甚至兩條桌子之間的距離 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這就是我們認為細胞決定在哪裡的動物在哪裡 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的樣子 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或在你車子上 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們要記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 他們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變形狀和大小的形狀和大小 , 就像我們在這個環境的形狀 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟如何改變形狀和大小環境的形狀 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小型平方環境下 , 就會看到 , 例如 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境大大 , 你會看到 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方環境大大 , 他們會認為旗幟在哪裡形成 , 但你讓環境更大了 , 他們認為旗幟在一個小型平方環境下 , 然後 , 如果你問他們 , 他們認為旗幟在一個小平方環境下進行 , 然後 , 如果你問他們 , 那
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	正如你所想像的 , 在那個位置的位置 , 那個位置在哪個位置上移動 , 然後你可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 ,
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這指導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們正在經歷運動 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 假如我們能整合這條路徑 , 不論是回到哪裡 , 我們都能整合這條路徑 , 應該要回到哪裡 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也會得到這種路徑融合 , 從一個細胞叫做網格細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞被發現 , 再次到海馬體 , 它們有點像細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在 , 當老鼠探險時 , 每個人的細胞都會在一個很奇妙的平行軌道上 , 繞著一系列不同的地點 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾種格格細胞的網格圖案中 , 每一個細胞的網格圖案 , 每個細胞的網格圖案就會轉移到其他細胞的網格 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的綠色在這個格子上 , 和綠色的一面 , 在這上面的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 結合起來 , 就像老鼠可以在地圖上找到一個虛擬的線條 , 用三角形 , 讓它可以在地圖上找到一個虛擬的線條 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電動活動可以從一個細胞傳送到下一個細胞去追蹤它的位置 , 所以它可以通過這些細胞來追蹤它的位置 , 讓它能在它的環境中移動 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於這些特定的神經活動 , 大腦中的特定部位可以改變根據 , 不論我們在哪個方向跑步 , 或跑到六個方向前 , 或跑到六個方向前 , 或跑到六個方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀裡 , 看看這個訊號 , 看看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你可以看到在人類的皮質上 , 這也是大腦的一部分 , 可以在腦中看到血管細胞 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車在哪個位置 , 距離和方向去延伸建築物和邊界的位置 , 讓他停下來 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會代表的是神經細胞的爆炸 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車輛停車場所取出的路徑 , 它會代表在網格細胞的路上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓細胞發燒 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到那個地方的位置 , 在那裡他停車的位置是最好的 , 和他在大腦中找到的那個地方的位置 , 和他停車的位置相比 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置遠遠的視覺形式 , 像是他的車子是否存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被困住了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道那是哪裡的 , 所以他知道它是怎麼回事 , 所以他知道那是什麼 , 所以他知道該怎麼做 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	超越空間記憶力 , 如果我們看看這個網格圖像在整個腦部運作時 , 我們會看到它在整整一系列的活動中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它 , 在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦中 , 我們看到它在整個大腦裡 , 我們看到它 ,
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是神經機制 , 顯示在我們周圍的環境中 , 可能是用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出視覺影像 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果發生了 , 你的記憶可以從各個細胞開始 , 藉由細胞來創造出你周圍的空間結構 , 來創造你周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 例如 , 我沒有提到 , 反射細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 他們火火就像是你所面臨的那樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看的方向 , 你可以想像你在這個事件發生的狀況 , 例如:你要在這個場景上產生一張影像 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以這只是一個新時代的認知神經元 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你如何記得或想像 , 甚至思考一下 , 大腦的數十億個個體神經元的活動 。

imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全局 , 由合作夥伴、政府、私人部門和公共部門所建構 , 不論是公共場所 , 都不是牆壁 , 而是詹姆斯•史塔利斯•史塔利斯•史密斯•史維斯 , 最好的信息 , 來自近期的軍事歷史來解釋為什麼安全的未來應該要建立橋樑 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作 , 全球議題 , 開放資源 , 公共和平 , 政治 , 社交媒體 , 暴力 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史維里: , 詹姆斯•史維里迪斯:那是如何對全球安全保持最高的主題 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談談開放式安全的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀得到更好的安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我開始說 , 咱們來回二十世紀 , 來看看二十世紀 , 這對我們來說是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是巴特 , 法國的北方 , 位於北方 , 位於北方的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年 , 約有70萬人被殺死 , 大約有20000天 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你在第二次世界大戰中 , 將它轉向二十世紀的安全 , 你就會看到戰爭 , 三百天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界戰爭的戰場開始 , 進入冷戰、伊朗的戰場 , 接著進入冷戰 , 進入冷戰 , 鐵柱 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	今天我對我們來說 , 不是要建立橋樑 , 而是要建立橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是大自然的橋樑 , 和巴爾幹半島的溝通 , 和巴爾幹半島的橋樑 , 和巴爾幹半島的一小部分 , 和巴爾幹大樓的破壞 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 幾十年來 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 開始看到這些團體 , 開始 , 來了解這些社區 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會爭論 , 公開資源安全是關聯國際、私人的公共空間 , 並且在社交網路上建立了安全 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球共同點 , 都被建立牆壁所包圍 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個水龍 , 很明顯 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一艘船 , 一艘船 , 橫跨印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它的結尾會在它的邊界線上 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	以防止海盜來襲擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy是極具威脅性的威脅 , 在印度洋裡 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	陰謀也非常活躍在馬拉克卡 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在瓜地內部活躍了 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是在全球運輸系統中數十億美元的破壞 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船員 , 500名馬丁爾斯特 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球常見的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到不同的海洋 , 網際網路海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩位年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 給他們超過十億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的二分之一 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在大英國的國內 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海 , 我們所知無止是極端的基礎元素 , 完全是極端的基礎 , 絕對是激進開放的基礎 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另外一件我擔心的事情是 , 全球性的威脅是被販賣的威脅 , 透過歐洲來到美國的威脅 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心古柯鹼來自東北的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心人口販賣 , 和販賣風險 。 最重要的 , 可能 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 和販賣風險 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	販賣大量在海洋中 , 同時也在全球共通點上 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴各位 , 這是一張非常高科技的美國海軍軍隊 , 用來阻止販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這可是毒品委員會的副作用 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它在南美的叢林中被建造 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們拿了六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種人口販賣的毒品 , 大規模毀滅的威脅 , 也是威脅全球公眾的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	咱們在阿富汗舉辦這場演講 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一場 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	890%的全球貧窮、鴉片和海洛因 , 都來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到 , 當然 , 恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是蓋達組織所在的位置 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的緊急狀況 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 恐怖主義擔憂了全球公共的一部分 , 我們必須處理 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 我們是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們二十世紀的工具並不能運作 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把安全帶給槍枝的安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會把安全帶到槍枝的安全之中 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要應用軍事力量 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這麼做時 , 我們一定要做得很好 , 並且競爭 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 公開資源安全是國際間、私人交流的連結 , 和私人交流的網際網路 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗 。
they are all holding books .	他們全都包含書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我以為我讀了這個人口統計 , 年輕的男性和女性 , 二十三十多歲 , 在阿富汗 , 很大 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%無法讀到阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班教育在那時候 , 那些男人和女人都可以學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以 , 問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們正在教導他們閱讀文學 , 與私人部門合作 , 和發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們教了超過200 , 000個阿富汗安全部隊 , 來閱讀和寫字 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你讀和寫在阿富汗時 , 你通常會把筆放在你的口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們拿著一筆很棒的驕傲 , 放進口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這裡有五十個國家參與這個任務 , 這些發展機構和私人公共部門 , 來處理這種安全性 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教他們對抗技能 , 但我會說 , 開放資源的安全感應是要建立更長的保障方式 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適 。

they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	此外 , 舒適圈 , 在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的cruis中 , 他們會有40萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它不是被軍事包裹起來的 , 而是由軍事組成 , 包括人道組織:手術希望、計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織把志工投入 。
interagency physicians come out .	醫師們走出來 。
they're all part of this .	它們都是這一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親兩天來到眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被送進時 , 他突然被看上去 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 維羅•伊斯維羅 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	乘以四十萬個病人治療 , 這種私人和安全的力量 , 你開始看到創造安全力量的力量 。

another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	另一方面的另一面是災難性的信仰 。

in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	每次在2004年25000000000000人死後 , 最嚴重的地震發生了2004年250 , 000個死者 , 海地基斯坦的地震 , 在巴基斯坦的兩萬五千人死亡 , 地震在巴基斯坦的恐怖襲擊日本和核能產業發生了 。 此時 , 我們看到各國際間的合作關係 , 國際間的交互作用 , 和其它核能產業所發生的一切 。

and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是 , 今天早上 , 我有幾百臉書的朋友 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 通常會說: 「 admire , 我們聽到你需要朋友 , 噢 , 誰 , 來吧 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	沒錯 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何傳達訊息 , 這樣傳達訊息 , 就是我們如何連結國際、私人和社交網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。

you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	這樣一來 , 我就想 , 要是哪個世紀安全、國際、私人和公共事業 , 兩一世紀的安全、國際、互相交流、國際、互相交流 , 會有多次的力量 。

the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的維基百科是非常簡單的:一個世界 , 每個人都可以自由地分享在所有的知識中 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的意思是 , 透過結合國際、互相、國際、互聯、私人的公共空間 , 在這個21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的安全性 。
